### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Health Alerts

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to store and manage automated alerts related to patient health, adherence, or critical events. Its primary business purpose is to notify healthcare providers (doctors) about situations requiring their attention or intervention, enabling proactive patient care and risk management.

KEY_ENTITIES:
The primary entity stored here is an **Alert**. Each alert pertains to a specific **Patient** and is relevant to an **Attending Doctor** or care team member.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: Unique identifier for each alert document.
*   `patient_id`: A foreign key referencing the `_id` of the patient who triggered or is associated with the alert. Essential for retrieving patient context.
*   `doctor_id`: A foreign key referencing the `_id` of the doctor responsible for or assigned to the patient, indicating who should be notified or act on the alert.
*   `alert_type`: Categorizes the nature of the alert (e.g., 'low_adherence', 'abnormal_vital'). Important for filtering and understanding the immediate issue.
*   `title`: A brief, human-readable summary of the alert.
*   `description`: A detailed explanation of the alert, often including specific measurements or events that triggered it.
*   `severity`: Indicates the urgency and potential impact of the alert (e.g., 'warning', 'critical'). Critical for prioritization by healthcare staff.
*   `status`: The current state of the alert (e.g., 'open', 'acknowledged', 'resolved'). Used for tracking the lifecycle and resolution progress.
*   `created_at`: Timestamp indicating when the alert was initially generated, crucial for understanding timeliness.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Patients Collection:** The `patient_id` field links directly to a `patients` collection (or similar, e.g., `users` with a patient role) to retrieve comprehensive patient demographic, medical history, and contact information.
*   **Doctors/Users Collection:** The `doctor_id` field links to a `doctors` or `users` collection to retrieve details about the responsible healthcare provider.
*   **Source Data Collections (Implicit):** Alerts are *triggered by* data residing in other collections, such as `vitals` (for `abnormal_vital` alerts), `medication_adherence` or `check_ins` (for `low_adherence` alerts), or `devices` (for device-related issues). While not directly referenced by an ID in the alert document, the `description` field often contains derived data from these sources.

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection supports a "Patient Monitoring and Intervention Workflow".
1.  **Automated Detection:** Background services or analytical pipelines continuously monitor patient data (e.g., vital signs, medication logs, check-in compliance) stored in other collections.
2.  **Alert Generation:** When predefined thresholds or conditions are met (e.g., blood pressure exceeds limits, patient misses a set number of check-ins), a new alert document is created in the `alerts` collection.
3.  **Notification and Triage:** Healthcare professionals (doctors, nurses) are notified of new alerts, often via a dashboard application that displays `open` alerts, prioritizing them by `severity`.
4.  **Review and Action:** The doctor reviews the alert details, including the `patient_id`, `alert_type`, `description`, and `severity`. They then decide on appropriate action, such as contacting the patient, adjusting treatment plans, or scheduling a follow-up.
5.  **Status Management:** As the doctor addresses the alert, its `status` is updated (e.g., from `open` to `acknowledged` and eventually to `resolved` or `closed`), providing an auditable trail of care and intervention.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE:
Appointment Visit Records

COLLECTION_PURPOSE:
This collection serves to track the real-world progression of a patient's visit for a scheduled appointment, from their physical check-in at a clinic to the completion of their visit. It acts as an operational log and status tracker for appointment fulfillment, providing critical timestamps and contextual links for billing, reporting, and workflow management.

KEY_ENTITIES:
The primary entity stored here is an **Appointment Check-in Event** or **Patient Visit Record**. This event links to several other core entities:
*   **Appointment**: The scheduled event for which the patient is checking in.
*   **Patient**: The individual who is attending the appointment.
*   **Doctor/Practitioner**: The healthcare provider associated with the appointment.
*   **Clinic/Facility**: The physical location where the appointment takes place.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: Unique identifier for this specific appointment check-in event.
*   `appointment_id`: A foreign key referencing the scheduled appointment document in an `appointments` collection. This links the check-in event to its pre-planned context.
*   `patient_id`: A foreign key referencing the patient's record in a `patients` collection. Identifies the individual attending.
*   `doctor_id`: A foreign key referencing the doctor's record in a `doctors` or `users` collection. Identifies the practitioner involved.
*   `clinic_id`: A foreign key referencing the clinic's record in a `clinics` or `facilities` collection. Specifies the location of the visit.
*   `checked_in_at`: A timestamp indicating when the patient officially arrived and checked in for their appointment. This marks the start of the physical visit.
*   `completed_at`: A timestamp indicating when the appointment visit was marked as finished (e.g., patient left, doctor signed off). This marks the end of the physical visit.
*   `status`: The current state of the check-in event (e.g., 'pending', 'checked_in', 'completed', 'no-show', 'cancelled').

RELATIONSHIPS:
This collection typically has the following relationships:
*   **One-to-One / One-to-Few** with an `appointments` collection via `appointment_id`. (One successful check-in per appointment, though an appointment might have multiple check-in *attempts* or a single appointment might map to multiple services/checkins).
*   **Many-to-One** with a `patients` collection via `patient_id`. (Many check-ins for one patient over time).
*   **Many-to-One** with a `doctors` (or `users`) collection via `doctor_id`. (Many check-ins involving one doctor).
*   **Many-to-One** with a `clinics` (or `facilities`) collection via `clinic_id`. (Many check-ins occurring at one clinic).

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection is foundational for managing the real-time patient flow and operational efficiency within a healthcare facility. It supports workflows such as:
1.  **Patient Arrival & Queue Management**: When a patient arrives, a record is created/updated with `checked_in_at`, allowing clinic staff to see who has arrived and is waiting.
2.  **Visit Status Tracking**: Provides real-time visibility into whether a patient has checked in, is currently with the doctor, or has completed their visit.
3.  **Operational Metrics & Reporting**: Enables calculation of key performance indicators such as wait times, visit duration, doctor utilization, and patient throughput.
4.  **Billing & Auditing**: The `checked_in_at` and `completed_at` timestamps can be crucial for accurate billing based on service duration or presence in the clinic, and for auditing visit histories.
5.  **No-Show/Cancellation Management**: The `status` field can be updated to reflect no-shows or cancellations, informing follow-up actions and scheduling adjustments.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Appointment Scheduling

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to record, manage, and track all scheduled appointments between patients and healthcare providers (doctors) at specific clinics. Its primary business purpose is to facilitate efficient scheduling, resource allocation, and historical tracking of patient visits within a healthcare system.

KEY_ENTITIES: The core entity stored here is an **Appointment**. Each document represents a single scheduled interaction, linking together the following related entities:
*   **Patient**: The individual receiving care.
*   **Doctor**: The healthcare professional providing care.
*   **Clinic**: The facility where the appointment takes place.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each individual appointment record.
*   `patient_id`: A reference to the patient participating in this appointment. Essential for retrieving patient-specific schedules.
*   `doctor_id`: A reference to the doctor assigned to this appointment. Critical for managing doctor's calendars and workload.
*   `clinic_id`: A reference to the clinic location where the appointment is held. Useful for clinic-specific scheduling and resource management.
*   `scheduled_at`: The exact date and time the appointment is scheduled to begin. This is fundamental for calendar views and time-based queries.
*   `status`: Indicates the current state of the appointment (e.g., 'scheduled', 'completed', 'cancelled', 'no-show'). Vital for workflow management and reporting.
*   `appointment_type`: Describes the nature of the appointment (e.g., 'consultation', 'follow-up', 'procedure', 'check-up'). Helps categorize and filter appointments.
*   `duration_minutes`: The planned length of the appointment, in minutes. Used for calculating availability and scheduling efficiency.
*   `title`: A brief, human-readable description or subject for the appointment.

RELATIONSHIPS: This collection primarily establishes relationships with other collections through its reference fields:
*   **`patient_id`**: Establishes a "many-to-one" relationship with a `patients` collection, where each patient can have many appointments.
*   **`doctor_id`**: Establishes a "many-to-one" relationship with a `doctors` collection, where each doctor can have many appointments.
*   **`clinic_id`**: Establishes a "many-to-one" relationship with a `clinics` collection, indicating where the appointment is taking place.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection is central to several key workflows in a healthcare management system:
1.  **Appointment Booking**: It stores new appointment requests and confirmed schedules for patients, doctors, and clinics.
2.  **Schedule Management**: It enables viewing, modifying, and canceling appointments for staff, doctors, and patients, providing a comprehensive calendar overview.
3.  **Patient Flow**: It tracks patient visits from scheduling to completion or cancellation, informing patient check-in/check-out processes.
4.  **Resource Utilization**: It helps clinics and doctors monitor their schedules, availability, and capacity.
5.  **Reporting and Analytics**: Provides data for operational reports on appointment volumes, no-show rates, doctor efficiency, and clinic activity.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: User Authentication Registry

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves as the central repository for user authentication credentials and core identity information within the Mediimate application. Its primary business purpose is to enable users to register, log in, and manage their basic account details securely, forming the foundation for all user-facing interactions.

KEY_ENTITIES: The core entity stored in this collection is a **User**. These users can represent various roles within the healthcare ecosystem, such as Patients, Doctors, Clinic Administrators, or System Administrators, as indicated by different email patterns and additional fields like `clinic_id` and `approval_status`.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: MongoDB's default unique identifier for each document.
*   `user_id`: A unique, application-level identifier (UUID) for the user. This is crucial for linking user data across various other collections in the system.
*   `email`: The user's unique email address, serving as a primary login credential and contact point.
*   `password_hash`: A securely hashed version of the user's password, used for authentication. It's vital that only hashes are stored, not plain text passwords.
*   `createdAt`, `updatedAt`: Timestamps indicating when the user record was created and last modified, important for auditing.
*   `email_verified`: A boolean field indicating whether the user's email address has been confirmed, enhancing account security and validity.
*   `clinic_id`: (Optional) A reference to a `clinic` collection, indicating that this user is associated with a specific clinic. This typically applies to doctors, nurses, or administrative staff.
*   `approval_status`: (Optional) A status field (e.g., 'active', 'approved', 'pending') used to manage the onboarding or operational status of certain user types, particularly those requiring administrative approval (e.g., doctors, clinic admins).

RELATIONSHIPS: This collection is foundational and has strong relationships with almost all other user-centric collections.
*   **`profiles` (or `patients`, `doctors`, `admins`) collections:** These would store richer, role-specific demographic and professional details (e.g., patient medical history, doctor's specialization, clinic address) and would link back to `authusers` using the `user_id`.
*   **`sessions` collection:** Stores active user sessions or authentication tokens, referencing `user_id` to maintain login state.
*   **`roles` or `user_roles` collections:** If a granular Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) system is implemented, it would link `user_id` to specific roles and permissions.
*   **`clinics` collection:** The `clinic_id` field directly references a `clinics` collection, associating staff and doctors with their respective healthcare facilities.
*   **Transaction/Activity Collections (e.g., `appointments`, `medical_records`, `billing`):** These would link to `user_id` to identify the patient or practitioner involved in specific records or activities.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a critical role in several core workflows:
1.  **User Registration & Account Creation:** When a new user signs up, their basic credentials (email, hashed password, `user_id`) are stored here.
2.  **User Login & Authentication:** It's the primary data source for validating user credentials during the login process by comparing submitted passwords with stored hashes.
3.  **Account Recovery (Password Reset):** The `email` field is essential for initiating password reset procedures and sending recovery links.
4.  **User Identity Verification:** The `email_verified` field supports the workflow of confirming a user's email address.
5.  **User Onboarding & Lifecycle Management:** Fields like `approval_status` facilitate workflows for approving or activating certain user accounts (e.g., doctors, clinic staff) after review.
6.  **Access Control Foundation:** By providing a unique `user_id` and potentially `clinic_id` or `approval_status`, it indirectly informs and enables role-based access control and personalized application experiences for different user types.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Care Plan Assignments & Daily Progress

COLLECTION_PURPOSE:
This collection serves as the central repository for tracking individual patients' progress and adherence to specific care plans. It captures the real-time operational state of each patient's journey through their assigned health regimen, including daily health metrics, activities, medication adherence, and engagement data, along with any triggered escalations. It's crucial for monitoring, intervention, and evaluating the effectiveness of care plans.

KEY_ENTITIES:
1.  **Care Plan Assignment**: The primary entity, representing a specific instance of a care plan tailored and assigned to a particular patient.
2.  **Daily Log (embedded)**: A sub-entity within each assignment, detailing the patient's reported activities and health measurements for a given day (e.g., sugar levels, medication intake, exercise).
3.  **MHP History (embedded)**: A sub-entity recording the points earned by a patient for various actions, supporting a gamification or incentive system.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: Unique identifier for this specific care plan assignment.
*   `patient_id`: References the associated patient document (e.g., in a `patients` collection). Critical for linking assignments to individual patients.
*   `careplan_id`: References the specific care plan template document (e.g., in a `careplans` collection). Essential for defining the plan's structure and goals.
*   `doctor_id`: References the doctor or healthcare provider responsible for overseeing this care plan assignment (e.g., in a `doctors` collection).
*   `status`: The current state of the assignment (e.g., 'active', 'completed', 'paused').
*   `start_date`: The date when the patient officially began this care plan assignment.
*   `current_day`: The current day number within the care plan sequence, reflecting progress.
*   `day_logs`: An embedded array of documents, where each document records daily activities and vital signs such as `fasting_sugar`, `postmeal_sugar`, `meds_taken`, `meals_logged`, `workout_logged`, `foot_check_done`, and `escalation_triggered`. This is the core of daily progress tracking.
*   `mhp_balance`, `mhp_tier`, `mhp_history`: Fields supporting a gamification or reward system, indicating accumulated points, reward level, and a detailed log of how points were earned. These incentivize patient engagement.
*   `escalations_count`, `escalation_log`: Records the number and details of critical events or alerts triggered during the care plan, indicating potential health risks or non-adherence.
*   `baseline_sugar`, `baseline_timing`: Initial health metrics recorded when the patient started the plan, used for comparison and measuring progress.
*   `medicines`: A list of medications prescribed as part of this specific care plan.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **One-to-Many (Patient to Care Plan Assignments)**: A `patient` (from a `patients` collection) can have multiple `careplanassignments` over time, although typically one active at a time for a specific condition.
*   **Many-to-One (Care Plan Template to Care Plan Assignments)**: Many `careplanassignments` can refer to the same `careplan_id` (from a `careplans` collection), as a care plan template can be assigned to many patients.
*   **Many-to-One (Doctor to Care Plan Assignments)**: Many `careplanassignments` can be overseen by the same `doctor_id` (from a `doctors` collection).
*   **Optional Many-to-One (Clinic to Care Plan Assignments)**: If `clinic_id` is populated, many `careplanassignments` might be associated with a specific `clinic` (from a `clinics` collection).
*   **Implicit Relationship to Appointments**: The `appointment_booked` field suggests a potential linkage or trigger for records in an `appointments` collection.

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection plays a critical role in the **patient care management and monitoring workflow**.
*   **Patient Onboarding**: Records the initiation and setup of a patient on a care plan.
*   **Daily Progress Tracking**: Captures granular daily data, enabling patients to log activities and measurements, and allowing healthcare providers to monitor adherence and health trends.
*   **Intervention and Escalation**: Facilitates identifying non-adherence or critical health deviations (`escalation_triggered`, `escalation_log`), prompting timely interventions by care teams.
*   **Patient Engagement**: Supports gamification and rewards systems (`mhp_balance`, `mhp_history`, `mhp_tier`) to motivate patients to stay engaged with their care plans.
*   **Outcomes Analysis**: Provides a historical record of patient activity and health metrics, essential for evaluating the effectiveness of care plans and patient outcomes over time.
*   **Reporting and Analytics**: Serves as a primary data source for dashboards, reports, and analytical insights into patient cohorts and care plan efficacy.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE:
Care Plan Definitions

COLLECTION_PURPOSE:
This collection serves as a catalog or template repository for structured chronic care programs. Its primary business purpose is to define and store the blueprints of various health management plans that can be offered to patients, specifying their duration, target conditions, activities, scoring rules for engagement, and associated rewards.

KEY_ENTITIES:
The key entity stored here is a **Care Plan Template** or **Program Definition**. It describes a generic, reusable structure for a specific health management program, not an instance assigned to a particular patient.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for this specific care plan definition.
*   `name`: A human-readable title for the care plan (e.g., "30-Day Diabetes Chronic Care Program").
*   `condition`: The medical condition that this care plan is designed to address (e.g., "Type 2 Diabetes"). Crucial for assigning relevant plans to patients.
*   `description`: A detailed explanation of the program's scope, goals, and activities.
*   `duration_days`: The intended length of the care plan in days.
*   `is_active`: A boolean flag indicating whether the care plan is currently available for enrollment.
*   `scoring_rules`: An embedded document that defines various patient actions (e.g., logging blood sugar, confirming medicine) and the corresponding "Medical Health Points" (MHP) awarded for each, driving patient engagement.
*   `reward_tiers`: An array of embedded documents outlining the different reward levels patients can achieve based on their accumulated MHP, incentivizing adherence and progress.
*   `week_themes`: An array of embedded documents detailing the thematic focus and goals for each week of the care plan, providing a structured progression for the patient journey.

RELATIONSHIPS:
This collection primarily defines *what* a care plan is. It likely relates to other collections as follows:
*   **Patient Enrollments/PatientCarePlans**: An intermediate collection linking a `patient_id` (from a `patients` or `users` collection) to a `careplan_id` (from *this* collection) and tracking the patient's individual progress within that plan (e.g., current MHP, start date, completion status). This would represent an *instance* of a care plan for a specific patient.
*   **Doctors/Providers**: Doctors or healthcare providers might be associated with creating, managing, or prescribing these care plans, possibly linked by `provider_id` or `doctor_id`.
*   **Activity Logs/Health Metrics**: The `scoring_rules` suggest that patient actions (e.g., `fasting_sugar_log`, `medicine_confirm`) are recorded in other collections (e.g., `health_logs`, `medication_records`). These logs would reference the rules defined here to update a patient's MHP in their enrolled care plan.
*   **Partners/Clinics**: Reward descriptions like "partner clinic" suggest a potential relationship with a `partners` or `clinics` collection, detailing information about associated healthcare facilities or reward providers.

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection plays a central role in several key workflows:
1.  **Care Plan Design and Management**: Allows healthcare organizations to define, configure, update, and activate/deactivate structured care programs for various conditions.
2.  **Patient Onboarding and Enrollment**: Serves as a library from which patients (or their clinicians) can select and enroll in specific health programs tailored to their diagnosed conditions.
3.  **Patient Engagement and Gamification**: Provides the underlying rules and reward structure that drives patient participation and adherence by tracking actions, awarding points (MHP), and enabling reward redemption.
4.  **Personalized Care Delivery**: Enables the system to assign and guide patients through a structured, progressive journey to manage their chronic conditions based on predefined weekly themes and goals.
5.  **Reporting and Analytics**: The defined plan structure and rules can be used as a baseline for measuring patient progress, program effectiveness, and overall engagement.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient AI Chat Transcripts

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves as the primary repository for storing all chat conversations between individual patients and an AI health assistant. Its purpose is to maintain a complete historical record of interactions, enabling the application to provide continuous context for ongoing conversations, track patient engagement, and facilitate analysis of AI performance and user needs.

KEY_ENTITIES:
*   **Conversation**: The core entity, representing a single, continuous dialogue session between a patient and the AI assistant.
*   **Message**: An embedded entity within a conversation, representing an individual turn of communication (either from the user/patient or the AI assistant).
*   **Patient**: Referenced by `patient_id`, indicating the individual participant in the conversation.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each chat conversation record.
*   `patient_id`: A reference ID linking the conversation to a specific patient. This is crucial for personalization and patient-specific history retrieval.
*   `messages`: An array of embedded documents, each representing a single message. This array forms the complete transcript of the conversation, ordered by `timestamp`.
    *   `messages.content`: The actual text of the message.
    *   `messages.role`: Indicates whether the message was sent by the 'user' (patient) or the 'assistant' (AI).
    *   `messages.timestamp`: The exact time the message was sent.
*   `created_at`: The timestamp when the conversation was initiated.
*   `last_activity`: The timestamp of the most recent message or activity within the conversation, useful for quickly identifying active or recent chats.
*   `source`: Indicates the origin of the conversation, typically 'chat'.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Patients Collection**: This collection directly links to a `patients` collection (or similar, e.g., `users`) via the `patient_id` field. This provides access to patient demographic information, health profiles, consent status, and other patient-specific data.
*   **AI Model/Analytics Logs (Potential)**: The `extracted_logs` field, though empty in samples, suggests a potential relationship or integration with a system that performs natural language processing (NLP) or analytics on conversations, possibly storing summaries, intent classifications, or sentiment analysis results either within this field or in a separate `conversation_analytics` collection.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection is fundamental to several key workflows:
*   **Real-time Patient-AI Interaction**: It supports the live chat interface, storing new messages as they occur and retrieving past messages to display the conversation history to the patient and provide context to the AI assistant.
*   **Conversation History Retrieval**: Allows patients or healthcare providers to review past interactions, understanding the advice given, questions asked, and patient's reported status over time.
*   **AI Context Management**: For stateless AI models, this collection serves as the memory, providing the full conversation history to inform subsequent AI responses, leading to more coherent and personalized interactions.
*   **Patient Engagement and Monitoring**: Enables tracking the frequency, duration, and topics of patient interactions, providing insights into patient engagement with the digital health platform.
*   **Performance Monitoring and Improvement**: Data from this collection can be used to evaluate the AI assistant's accuracy, helpfulness, and adherence to guidelines, informing future model improvements and training.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Clinic Staff Invitations

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: To manage and track invitations extended to individuals (e.g., doctors, nurses, administrative staff) to join a specific clinic within the system. It facilitates the onboarding process by recording invitation details, tracking their status (pending, accepted, expired), and enabling secure user registration and affiliation with a clinic.

KEY_ENTITIES:
1.  **Invitation**: The primary entity, representing a single invitation sent to an individual.
2.  **Invited User**: The individual targeted by the invitation, identified by their email and intended role.
3.  **Inviter User**: The existing user (e.g., clinic administrator) who initiated the invitation.
4.  **Clinic**: The organization or facility that the invited user is intended to join.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: A unique identifier for the invitation document.
*   `clinic_id`: References the unique ID of the clinic to which the user is invited. Essential for associating the invitation with a specific clinic.
*   `email`: The email address of the individual being invited. This will likely be their primary identifier for registration.
*   `invite_code`: A unique, typically short, code provided to the invitee to validate and complete their joining process.
*   `invited_by`: References the unique ID of the user who issued the invitation. Important for auditing and tracking who initiated the invitation.
*   `role`: The intended role (e.g., 'doctor', 'nurse', 'admin') the invited user will assume upon joining the clinic.
*   `status`: The current state of the invitation (e.g., 'pending', 'accepted', 'rejected', 'expired', 'revoked').
*   `created_at`, `updatedAt`: Timestamps indicating when the invitation was created and last modified.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **`clinic_id`** likely connects to the `_id` field in a `clinics` or `organizations` collection, identifying the specific clinic.
*   **`invited_by`** likely connects to the `_id` field in a `users` collection, identifying the user who sent the invitation.
*   Upon successful acceptance of an invitation (when `status` changes from 'pending' to 'accepted'), a new record (or an update to an existing one) would typically be made in a `users` collection, associating the invited `email` and `role` with the `clinic_id`.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a critical role in the user onboarding and clinic staffing workflow.
1.  **Invitation Initiation**: A clinic administrator (an existing user) initiates the process to invite a new staff member (e.g., a doctor). A new document is created in `clinicinvites` with `status: 'pending'`.
2.  **Invitation Delivery**: An email containing the `invite_code` is sent to the `email` address specified in the document.
3.  **User Registration/Joining**: The invited individual receives the email, uses the `invite_code` during their registration or login process, and confirms their intent to join the specified clinic with the given role.
4.  **Invitation Fulfillment**: Upon successful completion, the `status` field in the `clinicinvites` document is updated (e.g., to 'accepted'), and a new user account is created or linked in the `users` collection, establishing their affiliation with the `clinic_id`.
5.  **Tracking and Management**: Allows administrators to view all pending, accepted, or expired invitations, resend invitations, or revoke them if necessary.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Clinic Memberships

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to define the relationship between individual users and specific clinics, specifying which user belongs to which clinic and what their designated role is within that clinic. It acts as a central registry for clinic affiliations and role-based access control.

KEY_ENTITIES: This collection primarily stores the *membership* entity, which is a join between:
*   **Users**: Individuals who interact with the system (e.g., staff, doctors, patients, administrators).
*   **Clinics**: Healthcare facilities or organizational units.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each membership record within this collection.
*   `clinic_id`: A reference (likely an ObjectId or UUID) to a specific clinic. This links a membership entry to a particular healthcare facility.
*   `user_id`: A reference (likely a UUID) to a specific user. This links a membership entry to a particular individual.
*   `role`: A string indicating the user's role within the specified clinic (e.g., 'owner', 'admin', 'doctor', 'patient', 'staff'). This field is critical for implementing role-based access control (RBAC).
*   `joined_at`: A timestamp indicating when the user was assigned this role or became a member of this clinic.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **`user_id`**: This field is a foreign key referencing a `users` collection (or `accounts`, `personnel`, etc.) where user details are stored.
*   **`clinic_id`**: This field is a foreign key referencing a `clinics` collection (or `healthcare_facilities`, `organizations`, etc.) where clinic details are stored.
*   This collection effectively creates a many-to-many relationship between `users` and `clinics`, allowing a user to be associated with multiple clinics and a clinic to have multiple users.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a crucial role in several key workflows:
*   **User Onboarding/Offboarding**: When a new user joins a clinic or an existing user leaves, a record is created or updated/deleted here.
*   **Access Control and Authorization**: When a user attempts to perform an action within a clinic's context, this collection is queried to determine if the user is a member of that clinic and what their `role` is, thereby enforcing permissions (e.g., only 'owner' or 'admin' can change clinic settings).
*   **Listing Clinic Staff/Members**: To display all users associated with a particular clinic and their respective roles.
*   **Listing User's Clinics**: To display all clinics a specific user is associated with.
*   **Clinic Administration**: For managing users and their roles within a clinic from an administrative interface.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Healthcare Clinics and Facilities

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves as a comprehensive registry for healthcare facilities such as clinics and hospitals. Its primary business purpose is to store and manage detailed information about these providers, enabling discovery, comparison, and administrative oversight within a healthcare management or patient-facing platform. It provides the foundational data for patients to find suitable care, and for the platform to manage its network of providers.

KEY_ENTITIES: Each document in this collection represents a single **Healthcare Clinic** or **Medical Facility**.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each clinic within the database.
*   `name`: The official name of the healthcare facility (e.g., "Mediimate Care Clinic", "Prashant clinic").
*   `address`: The physical street address of the clinic.
*   `phone`: The primary contact phone number for the clinic.
*   `email`: The primary contact email address for the clinic.
*   `specialties`: An array of medical specialties or services offered by the clinic (e.g., 'General Medicine', 'Cardiology').
*   `bed_count`: (Optional) The number of inpatient beds available, indicating facility size and capacity.
*   `opd_capacity`: (Optional) The outpatient department capacity, indicating the number of patients that can be seen daily.
*   `createdAt`, `updatedAt`: Timestamps indicating when the clinic record was created and last modified, important for auditing.
*   `created_by`: A UUID referencing the user or system that initially created this clinic's record, useful for tracking data origin and responsibility.
*   `international_support`: (Optional, embedded document) Details services offered for international patients, such as visa or travel assistance, showing a focus on global patient care.
*   `rating_avg`, `total_reviews`: (Optional) Aggregated metrics reflecting patient feedback and satisfaction, crucial for patient decision-making.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **`users` / `admins` collection (Many-to-One):** The `created_by` field likely references a `_id` from a `users` or `admins` collection, indicating the platform user or administrator responsible for creating/managing the clinic's profile.
*   **`doctors` collection (One-to-Many / Many-to-Many):** Clinics are primary workplaces for doctors. A `doctors` collection would likely include a `clinic_id` (for a doctor working at one clinic) or an array `clinic_ids` (for a doctor working at multiple clinics), referencing `clinics._id`.
*   **`appointments` collection (One-to-Many):** Patient appointments are made at specific clinics. An `appointments` collection would have a `clinic_id` field to link to the facility where the appointment takes place.
*   **`reviews` collection (One-to-Many):** The `rating_avg` and `total_reviews` fields imply a separate `reviews` collection where patients submit detailed feedback, each review containing a `clinic_id` reference.
*   **`specialties` / `treatments` lookup collections (Many-to-Many implied):** While `specialties` and `treatments_offered` are embedded as strings, they could ideally link to dedicated lookup collections for standardized medical categories and treatment definitions.
*   **`programs` collection (Many-to-Many):** The `program_ids` field suggests that clinics can participate in or offer specific health programs, linking to a `programs` collection that defines these offerings.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a critical role in supporting several key workflows:
1.  **Clinic Onboarding and Profile Management:** It allows administrators or clinic representatives to register new healthcare facilities and maintain their detailed profiles, including contact information, services, capacities, and accreditation details.
2.  **Patient Search and Discovery:** It enables patients to search for clinics based on various criteria such as location, specialties, facilities, and patient ratings, facilitating the process of finding suitable healthcare providers.
3.  **Appointment Booking Integration:** It provides the essential location and service context for appointment scheduling systems, linking patients to specific clinics for their consultations or procedures.
4.  **Referral System Support:** It serves as the data source for systems that refer patients to specialized clinics or facilities based on their medical needs.
5.  **Operational Reporting and Analytics:** Data within this collection (e.g., bed count, OPD capacity, specialties) can be used for platform-level reporting on provider network coverage, resource availability, and service distribution.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Prospective Customer Inquiries

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to capture and manage information about individuals or organizations who have expressed initial interest in a product or service. It acts as the primary repository for "leads" generated through various channels, typically online forms (e.g., free trial requests, contact forms), facilitating their initial processing and subsequent follow-up by sales or marketing teams.

KEY_ENTITIES: Each document in this collection represents a **Lead** or a **Prospective Client/Customer**. It's a record of an individual or entity that has initiated contact and shown potential interest in the business's offerings.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each lead record within MongoDB.
*   `name`: The full name of the individual submitting the inquiry.
*   `email`: The email address provided by the lead for contact.
*   `phone`: The phone number provided by the lead for contact.
*   `type`: Indicates the nature of the inquiry or the lead's expressed interest (e.g., 'free_trial' suggests interest in evaluating the service).
*   `source`: Specifies the origin of the lead (e.g., 'website'), crucial for tracking marketing channel effectiveness.
*   `message`: A free-text field for any additional message, question, or specific request from the lead.
*   `clinic_name`: (Optional) The name of a clinic, suggesting a potential B2B focus where clinics are the target clients.
*   `gsheet_synced`: A boolean flag indicating whether this lead's data has been successfully synchronized to a Google Sheet, likely for external tracking, assignment, or manual sales process management.
*   `createdAt`: Timestamp recording when the lead record was first created.
*   `updatedAt`: Timestamp recording when the lead record was last modified.
*   `__v`: Mongoose version key, used for internal document versioning.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Users/Customers Collection**: Once a lead converts into a paying customer or active user, their core information would typically be moved or linked to a `Users` or `Customers` collection. The `_id` from this collection might be stored in the `Users` document to maintain a historical link.
*   **CRM Activities/Interactions Collection**: Subsequent interactions with the lead (e.g., sales calls, emails, demo scheduled) would likely be stored in a separate `CRMActivities` or `Interactions` collection, referencing the `_id` of the lead from this collection.
*   **Marketing Campaigns Collection**: The `source` field could potentially link to a `MarketingCampaigns` collection to provide detailed context about the specific campaign that generated the lead, allowing for deeper analysis of marketing ROI.
*   **Analytics & Reporting Systems**: Data from this collection is frequently fed into business intelligence tools or data warehouses to analyze lead generation performance, conversion rates, and sales funnel effectiveness.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection is central to the **initial stages of the Sales & Marketing Funnel**.
1.  **Lead Generation**: It acts as the intake mechanism for capturing interest from potential customers who fill out forms (e.g., "Request Free Trial") on the company's website or other digital touchpoints.
2.  **Lead Nurturing & Qualification**: New entries in this collection trigger follow-up actions. Sales or marketing teams access this data to contact leads, qualify their needs, and move them through the sales pipeline. The `gsheet_synced` flag suggests an integration point for further external processing or manual assignment workflows.
3.  **Performance Tracking**: Marketing teams utilize fields like `source` and `type` to analyze the effectiveness of different lead generation strategies and channels.
4.  **Conversion Monitoring**: Leads are tracked in this collection until they either convert into active users/customers (and potentially migrate to another collection) or are deemed unqualified.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Doctor Recurring Availability Schedules

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection defines the recurring weekly time blocks during which doctors are generally available for appointments. It serves as the foundational data for generating potential appointment slots on a calendar, based on each doctor's standard working hours and preferred appointment types. It does not store actual booked appointments but rather the rules for when appointments *can* be booked.

KEY_ENTITIES: The primary entity stored here is a "Doctor's Weekly Availability Rule" or "Recurring Schedule Block." Each document represents a specific time window on a particular day of the week when a doctor is available to see patients, potentially at a specific clinic and for specific types of appointments.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for this specific availability rule document.
*   `doctor_id`: A unique identifier (UUID) linking this availability rule to a specific doctor. Essential for knowing whose schedule this applies to.
*   `day_of_week`: An integer representing the day of the week (e.g., 0 for Sunday, 1 for Monday, etc.), indicating on which recurring day this availability applies.
*   `start_time`: A string representing the start time of the availability block for the `day_of_week` (e.g., "09:00").
*   `end_time`: A string representing the end time of the availability block for the `day_of_week` (e.g., "17:00").
*   `slot_duration_minutes`: An integer indicating the default duration of individual bookable slots within this availability block (e.g., 15, 30, 45 minutes).
*   `appointment_types`: An array of strings listing the types of appointments that can be booked during this availability block (e.g., "consultation", "follow_up"). An empty array implies any valid appointment type might be allowed, or it's implicitly defined elsewhere.
*   `is_active`: A boolean flag indicating whether this availability rule is currently active and should be considered for generating appointment slots.
*   `clinic_id` (optional): A unique identifier linking this availability rule to a specific clinic location. This is crucial for doctors who work across multiple clinics, defining their schedule per location.
*   `createdAt`, `updatedAt`: Timestamps indicating when the availability rule was created and last modified.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **`doctors` collection**: The `doctor_id` field is a direct reference to a document in a `doctors` collection, which would hold detailed information about each medical practitioner (e.g., name, specialty, contact info).
*   **`clinics` collection**: The `clinic_id` field (when present) is a direct reference to a document in a `clinics` collection, detailing information about specific clinic locations (e.g., address, contact info).
*   **`appointments` collection**: This collection serves as input for generating potential slots that populate an `appointments` collection. When a patient books an appointment, the system queries `doctoravailabilities` to determine *when* a doctor is available, then creates an entry in `appointments` for the specific time slot, effectively consuming a portion of the doctor's recurring availability for a particular date.
*   **`appointment_types` or `services` collection**: The `appointment_types` array likely refers to a master list of predefined appointment types (e.g., in a `service_types` or `appointment_types` collection) to ensure consistency and provide details about each type.
*   **`doctor_exceptions` or `doctor_leaves` collection**: This collection defines *regular* availability. An `appointments` or scheduling system would likely also consult a separate collection for ad-hoc schedule changes, holidays, or leave (e.g., `doctor_leaves`, `doctor_exceptions`) to override or block out parts of these recurring availabilities on specific dates.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a central role in the core appointment scheduling workflow.
1.  **Doctor/Admin Schedule Setup**: Allows doctors or administrative staff to define a doctor's standard weekly working hours and specific time blocks for different appointment types.
2.  **Patient Appointment Booking**: When a patient searches for an available slot, the system queries this collection (filtered by `doctor_id`, `clinic_id`, `appointment_types`, and `is_active`) to identify potential recurring time slots. It then projects these recurring availabilities onto specific dates, factoring in the `slot_duration_minutes`, and cross-references with already booked appointments and doctor exceptions to present actual bookable slots to the patient.
3.  **Calendar Generation**: It's used by the system to dynamically generate a doctor's weekly or monthly calendar view, showing their general working hours before any specific appointments are booked.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Email Notification Log

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: To provide a comprehensive and immutable record of all email notifications sent by the "Mediimate" application. This serves as an audit trail for system communications, enables troubleshooting of delivery issues, supports customer service inquiries regarding sent emails, and provides historical data for communication analysis and compliance.

KEY_ENTITIES: The primary entity stored in this collection is an **Email Notification Event**. Each document represents a single instance of an email being sent by the system. These events are associated with **Users** or **Doctors** (the recipients) within the Mediimate platform.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each email notification log entry. Standard MongoDB `ObjectId`.
*   `sent_at`: A timestamp indicating the exact date and time when the email was sent. Crucial for chronological tracking and auditing.
*   `status`: The current delivery status of the email, typically 'sent' as seen in the samples. In a more advanced system, this could also track 'failed', 'pending', 'bounced', etc.
*   `template`: The name of the specific email template used to generate the email content (e.g., 'verification', 'welcome', 'doctor_approved', 'consultation_summary'). This field categorizes the type and purpose of the communication.
*   `subject`: The subject line of the email that was sent. Provides immediate context for the communication.
*   `to_email`: The email address of the intended recipient. Essential for identifying who received the communication.
*   `to_user_id`: (Optional) A UUID (Universally Unique Identifier) referencing the internal ID of the user or doctor within the Mediimate platform who received the email. This field directly links the email log to a specific user account. Its optionality suggests some emails might be sent to addresses not yet associated with a full user profile (e.g., initial invites).
*   `updatedAt`: A timestamp for the last update to the document. Often identical to `sent_at` if the document is created upon sending and not updated later.
*   `__v`: (Mongoose specific) A version key used for optimistic locking to prevent concurrent updates from overwriting each other.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Users/Accounts Collection**: The `to_user_id` field creates a direct foreign key-like relationship to a `users` or `accounts` collection (and potentially separate `doctors` and `patients` collections) to identify the specific individual who received the email.
*   **Email Templates Collection/Configuration**: The `template` field implies the existence of a separate collection, configuration, or service that defines the content, structure, and parameters for various types of email templates used by the application.
*   **Appointments/Consultations Collection**: For templates like `consultation_summary`, there is an indirect relationship to `appointments` or `consultations` collections, as these emails are triggered by and summarize events recorded there.
*   **Doctor Profiles Collection**: The `doctor_approved` template suggests a relationship with a `doctors` collection where doctor registration and approval statuses are managed.
*   **User Verification/Auth Tokens Collection**: Verification emails (`template: 'verification'`) would relate to a collection managing verification tokens or user activation states.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a vital role across multiple operational workflows within the Mediimate platform:
*   **User Onboarding and Activation**: Records verification and welcome emails sent to new users or doctors, confirming successful initiation of their accounts.
*   **Doctor Profile Management**: Logs approval notifications to doctors, indicating their profile activation.
*   **Patient-Doctor Interaction**: Archives summary emails related to consultations, ensuring a record of communication post-appointment.
*   **Customer Support & Troubleshooting**: Allows support staff to verify if a specific email (e.g., password reset, appointment reminder) was sent to a user, helping diagnose user issues.
*   **Auditing and Compliance**: Provides a verifiable history of user communication, essential for legal and regulatory compliance in healthcare platforms.
*   **System Reliability Monitoring**: Helps developers and operations teams debug email sending failures or delays by providing a log of attempted and successful sends.
*   **User Engagement & Marketing Analysis**: Can be used to analyze communication patterns, template effectiveness, and overall user engagement with the platform's notifications.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Program Enrollments

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to track and manage the specific instances of patients enrolling in and participating in various healthcare or wellness programs. It records the details of each enrollment, including the involved patient, the program itself, the supervising doctor, the enrollment timeline, and the patient's progress or status within the program.

KEY_ENTITIES:
While each document represents an *Enrollment* record, it fundamentally links three core entities:
1.  **Patient**: The individual undergoing the program.
2.  **Program**: The specific health or wellness initiative the patient is enrolled in.
3.  **Doctor**: The healthcare provider responsible for overseeing the patient's participation in the program.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for this specific enrollment record.
*   `patient_id`: A reference (likely ObjectId or UUID) to the specific patient entity.
*   `program_id`: A reference (likely ObjectId or UUID) to the program definition entity.
*   `doctor_id`: A reference (likely UUID) to the supervising doctor entity.
*   `enrolled_at`: A timestamp indicating when the patient officially joined the program.
*   `status`: The current state of the enrollment (e.g., 'active', 'completed', 'cancelled', 'paused').
*   `adherence_pct`: A percentage reflecting the patient's compliance or engagement with the program's requirements (e.g., medication intake, exercise completion). This is an important performance metric.
*   `completed_at`: A timestamp indicating when the patient successfully completed the program. This field is typically present when `status` is 'completed'.
*   `created_at`: Standard timestamp for when this enrollment record was first created.
*   `updatedAt`: Standard timestamp for the last modification of this enrollment record.

RELATIONSHIPS:
This collection acts as a join or linking collection, establishing relationships between three primary entities:
*   **`patient_id`**: Establishes a foreign key-like relationship to a `patients` collection, where detailed patient information (name, demographics, medical history) would reside.
*   **`program_id`**: Establishes a foreign key-like relationship to a `programs` collection, which would contain definitions and details of each program offered (e.g., program name, description, duration, objectives).
*   **`doctor_id`**: Establishes a foreign key-like relationship to a `doctors` or `users` collection, providing details about the supervising medical professional.

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection supports several critical real-world workflows in a healthcare or wellness management system:
1.  **Patient Onboarding/Enrollment**: When a patient is assigned or chooses to participate in a new program, a new document is created in this collection to record the enrollment.
2.  **Program Monitoring and Management**: Doctors and administrators use this collection to see which patients are active in which programs, track their progress, and monitor adherence.
3.  **Performance Tracking**: It enables the calculation and display of patient adherence, helping identify those who might need intervention or support.
4.  **Program Completion/Exit**: When a patient finishes a program, the `status` is updated to 'completed' and `completed_at` is recorded.
5.  **Reporting and Analytics**: Provides the foundation for reports on program participation rates, completion rates, doctor caseloads, and overall program effectiveness.
6.  **Doctor-Patient Program Assignment**: Clearly defines which doctor is responsible for overseeing a patient's journey through a specific program.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Feedback Invitations

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to manage and track the lifecycle of requests sent to patients to provide feedback on their appointments or interactions. It ensures that feedback invitations are properly recorded, linked to relevant entities, and their status can be monitored.

KEY_ENTITIES: The primary entity stored here is a **Feedback Request** or **Feedback Invitation**. Each document represents a unique instance of a request sent to a specific patient regarding a particular appointment, intended to gather their feedback.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for this specific feedback request document.
*   `appointment_id`: A foreign key linking this feedback request to the specific appointment for which feedback is being solicited. Crucial for context.
*   `patient_id`: A foreign key linking to the patient who is being asked to provide feedback.
*   `patient_user_id`: A foreign key linking to the patient's user account, likely used for sending the invitation (e.g., email address associated with the user).
*   `doctor_id`: A foreign key linking to the doctor involved in the appointment.
*   `token`: A unique, secure string used as an access key for the patient to submit feedback, typically embedded in a feedback survey URL.
*   `status`: The current state of the feedback request (e.g., 'submitted', 'pending', 'completed', 'expired', 'canceled').
*   `created_at`: Timestamp when this feedback request record was initially created in the system.
*   `submitted_at`: Timestamp when the feedback request (e.g., email/SMS with the link) was actually sent to the patient.
*   `expires_at`: Timestamp indicating when the feedback request token or link will become invalid, after which feedback can no longer be submitted through this request.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **`appointments` collection**: Linked via `appointment_id`, providing details about the specific patient visit.
*   **`patients` collection**: Linked via `patient_id`, providing demographic and medical information about the patient.
*   **`users` collection**: Linked via `patient_user_id`, providing user account details, potentially including contact information for sending the request.
*   **`doctors` collection**: Linked via `doctor_id`, providing details about the healthcare provider.
*   **`feedback` or `survey_responses` collection (implicit)**: This collection initiates the process, and an eventual feedback submission would likely be stored in a separate collection, referencing this `feedbackrequests` document or its `token`.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection is central to the **post-appointment patient feedback and quality improvement workflow**.
1.  **Trigger**: After an appointment (`appointment_id`) is marked as completed, a new feedback request document is generated.
2.  **Invitation**: A unique `token` is created, and an invitation (e.g., email or SMS) containing a link with this `token` is sent to the `patient_user_id`. The `status` is updated to 'submitted'.
3.  **Tracking & Expiry**: The system tracks the `status` of the request. If the `expires_at` timestamp is reached and no feedback has been submitted, the request can be marked as 'expired'.
4.  **Feedback Submission**: When a patient uses the `token` to submit feedback, the associated feedback is stored in a separate collection, and this request's `status` would likely be updated to 'completed'.
5.  **Reporting**: It enables reporting on feedback invitation rates, completion rates, and identifies opportunities for improving patient engagement and service quality.

====================================================================================================
COLLECTION: feedbacks

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Appointment Feedback

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: To capture, store, and manage structured feedback and ratings provided by patients following their medical appointments. This data serves to assess service quality, evaluate doctor performance, and potentially generate public testimonials.

KEY_ENTITIES: This collection primarily stores "Patient Feedback Records". Each document represents a single instance of feedback given by a patient regarding a specific doctor and appointment.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for this specific feedback record.
*   `appointment_id`: A reference to the particular appointment for which the feedback was given.
*   `patient_id`: A reference to the patient who submitted the feedback.
*   `doctor_id`: A reference to the doctor who is the subject of the feedback.
*   `doctor_rating`: A numerical rating (e.g., 1-5 stars) provided by the patient for the doctor.
*   `review_text`: The textual comments or detailed observations written by the patient.
*   `consent_to_publish`: A boolean flag indicating if the patient has granted permission for this feedback to be publicly displayed (e.g., on a doctor's profile page or testimonial section).
*   `feedback_request_id`: (Optional) A reference to the specific request or prompt that initiated this feedback submission, indicating a feedback solicitation process.
*   `created_at`, `updatedAt`: Timestamps indicating when the feedback was created and last modified.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **One-to-One/Many-to-One with `appointments` collection:** Links via `appointment_id` to retrieve details about the specific appointment the feedback pertains to.
*   **Many-to-One with `patients` collection:** Links via `patient_id` to the patient's profile or demographic information.
*   **Many-to-One with `doctors` collection:** Links via `doctor_id` to the doctor's profile or professional details.
*   **One-to-One/Many-to-One with `feedback_requests` collection (implied):** Links via `feedback_request_id` to a collection managing the lifecycle of feedback solicitation (if such a system exists).

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection is critical in the **Post-Appointment Feedback and Quality Assurance Workflow**. It facilitates the collection and storage of patient experiences after a medical service. This data is then used to:
1.  **Monitor Doctor Performance:** Aggregate ratings and reviews help assess individual doctor effectiveness and patient satisfaction.
2.  **Improve Service Quality:** Identify common themes or issues in `review_text` to pinpoint areas for operational improvements across the platform or specific clinics.
3.  **Support Patient Engagement:** Provides a channel for patients to express their opinions and contribute to service improvement.
4.  **Generate Testimonials/Marketing Content:** With `consent_to_publish`, positive feedback can be utilized for marketing purposes to attract new patients or build trust.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Dietary Intake Records

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection stores detailed logs of meals consumed by patients, including nutritional information (calories, macronutrients), meal type, and timestamps. Its primary business purpose is to enable monitoring, analysis, and management of patient dietary habits, supporting healthcare providers (doctors, dietitians) in assessing nutritional intake, adherence to diet plans, and making informed health recommendations.

KEY_ENTITIES:
*   **Food Log / Meal Entry**: The central entity, representing a single instance of a patient consuming a meal.
*   **Patient**: Each food log is associated with a specific patient who consumed the meal.
*   **Doctor**: Each food log is associated with a doctor, likely the one overseeing the patient's care or diet.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each individual food log entry.
*   `patient_id`: A reference to the patient who logged this meal. Critical for associating logs with specific individuals.
*   `doctor_id`: A reference to the doctor associated with this log, indicating oversight or responsibility.
*   `logged_at`: The specific date and time when the meal was consumed. Essential for chronological analysis and dietary patterns.
*   `meal_type`: Categorization of the meal (e.g., 'breakfast', 'lunch', 'dinner'), useful for understanding eating schedules.
*   `total_calories`, `total_carbs`, `total_fat`, `total_protein`: Key nutritional metrics summarizing the meal. These are central to dietary assessment.
*   `source`: Indicates how the food log was recorded (e.g., 'manual' suggests patient input). Useful for auditing and understanding data origin.
*   `created_at`, `updatedAt`: Timestamps indicating when the log entry was created and last modified in the system.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **patients collection**: `patient_id` is a foreign key referencing the `_id` of a document in a `patients` (or `users`) collection, which would contain patient demographic, medical, and contact information.
*   **doctors collection**: `doctor_id` is a foreign key referencing the `_id` of a document in a `doctors` (or `users`) collection, which would hold doctor profiles and credentials.
*   **dietPlans/nutritionGoals collection (Likely)**: While not directly linked by an ID in the sample, this collection would logically relate to a collection storing prescribed diet plans or nutritional goals for patients, allowing for comparison and progress tracking.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a vital role in healthcare and wellness applications that involve dietary management. It supports workflows such as:
1.  **Patient Self-Logging**: Patients use a mobile app or portal to manually log their meals throughout the day.
2.  **Doctor/Dietitian Review**: Healthcare providers access these logs to review a patient's dietary habits, assess adherence to diet plans, and identify potential issues or areas for improvement.
3.  **Nutritional Assessment & Feedback**: The aggregated nutritional data (calories, macros) allows for comprehensive analysis of a patient's intake over time, enabling personalized feedback and adjustments to treatment plans.
4.  **Health Outcome Correlation**: Data from this collection can be combined with other health metrics (e.g., weight, blood glucose) to understand the impact of diet on overall health outcomes.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Lab Reports

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves as a central repository for storing and managing patient laboratory test results. Its primary purpose is to capture uploaded lab report documents, extract key information, generate both medical-professional and patient-friendly summaries using AI, and facilitate the review and understanding of these results by doctors and patients. It supports efficient access, interpretation, and historical tracking of a patient's diagnostic data.

KEY_ENTITIES:
*   **Lab Report**: The core entity, representing a single set of laboratory test results for a specific patient at a particular time.
*   **Patient**: The individual for whom the lab tests were performed, identified by `patient_id`.
*   **Doctor/Uploader**: The medical professional or system user associated with the report, either as the ordering physician, reviewing doctor, or the entity responsible for uploading the report (`doctor_id`, `uploaded_by`).

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each lab report document within the collection.
*   `patient_id`: A foreign key linking this report to a specific patient. Essential for retrieving all reports for a given patient.
*   `doctor_id`: A foreign key linking this report to a specific doctor, likely the physician who ordered or is responsible for reviewing the report.
*   `tested_at`: The date and time when the laboratory tests were conducted, critical for chronological tracking and comparison of results over time.
*   `file_name`, `file_path`, `file_type`: Metadata and location information for the original digital lab report document (e.g., PDF).
*   `ai_summary`: An AI-generated summary of the lab results, tailored for medical professionals, highlighting key findings and potential implications.
*   `layman_summary`: An AI-generated simplified summary of the lab results, intended for patients to understand their health status in an accessible manner.
*   `extracted_data`: (Optional) Structured data parsed directly from the lab report, potentially including specific test values, normal ranges, and chart-ready data, enabling programmatic analysis and visualization.
*   `uploaded_by`: The ID of the user or system component that initiated the upload of the lab report.
*   `created_at`, `updatedAt`: Timestamps tracking the document's creation and last modification.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Patients Collection**: The `patient_id` field establishes a many-to-one relationship with a `patients` collection (or similar patient demographics collection), where detailed patient information resides.
*   **Doctors/Users Collection**: The `doctor_id` and `uploaded_by` fields establish many-to-one relationships with a `doctors` or `users` collection, storing details about medical practitioners and system users.
*   **Potentially other clinical data collections**: Lab reports are often ordered as part of a patient encounter or treatment plan, suggesting implicit or explicit links to `appointments`, `encounters`, or `treatment_plans` collections, depending on the overall system architecture.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection is integral to several critical healthcare workflows:
1.  **Lab Result Dissemination & Review**: Facilitates the secure storage and delivery of lab results to doctors, enabling them to quickly review and understand patient diagnostic data, often enhanced by AI summaries.
2.  **Patient Education & Engagement**: Provides easily understandable `layman_summary` directly to patients, empowering them to comprehend their health status and participate more actively in their care.
3.  **Clinical Decision Support**: AI summaries can highlight critical values or trends, assisting doctors in making timely and informed diagnostic and treatment decisions.
4.  **Historical Data Tracking & Trend Analysis**: Stores a chronological record of lab tests, allowing clinicians to monitor disease progression, evaluate treatment efficacy, and identify long-term health trends.
5.  **Integration with EHR/EMR Systems**: The `extracted_data` (if populated) can be used to populate structured fields within Electronic Health Records (EHR) or Electronic Medical Records (EMR) systems, or to power patient portals.
6.  **Document Management**: Serves as a digital archive for original lab report documents, ensuring their availability for reference or regulatory compliance.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Lab Results

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection stores individual diagnostic test results for patients. Its primary business purpose is to provide a comprehensive record of a patient's laboratory examinations, enabling medical professionals to diagnose conditions, monitor treatment effectiveness, track disease progression, and make informed clinical decisions.

KEY_ENTITIES:
The primary entity stored in this collection is a **Lab Result**. Each document represents a single outcome of a specific medical test performed on a patient at a given time.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each individual lab result record.
*   `patient_id`: A foreign key referencing the patient for whom the test was performed, crucial for associating results with the correct individual.
*   `doctor_id`: A foreign key referencing the doctor who ordered or is responsible for reviewing this specific lab test.
*   `test_name`: The descriptive name of the diagnostic test performed (e.g., 'HbA1c', 'Fasting Glucose', 'Total Cholesterol').
*   `result_value`: The actual measured or observed value obtained from the lab test.
*   `unit`: The unit of measurement for the `result_value` (e.g., '%', 'mg/dL').
*   `reference_range`: The expected or normal range of values for this specific test, used by clinicians to interpret whether the `result_value` is within healthy limits or indicates an anomaly.
*   `status`: The current state of the lab result, such as 'final' (indicating the result is validated and complete), 'pending', or 'corrected'.
*   `tested_at`: The timestamp indicating when the lab test was physically conducted.
*   `created_at`: The timestamp when this lab result record was first added to the system.
*   `updatedAt`: The timestamp when this lab result record was last modified in the system.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Patients**: This collection has a strong "many-to-one" relationship with a `patients` collection via `patient_id`. Each lab result belongs to one patient, and a patient can have many lab results.
*   **Doctors/Users**: It likely has a "many-to-one" relationship with a `doctors` or `users` collection via `doctor_id`, linking the lab result to the ordering or responsible physician.
*   **Test Catalog/Definitions**: Could implicitly relate to a `medical_tests` or `test_catalog` collection, where `test_name`, `unit`, and `reference_range` for standard tests might be defined.
*   **Appointments/Orders**: Potentially linked to a `medical_appointments` or `lab_orders` collection, if tests are ordered as part of an appointment or specific lab requisition.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection supports the core workflow of **Diagnostic Test Processing and Review**.
1.  **Test Ordering**: A doctor (referenced by `doctor_id`) orders lab tests for a patient (referenced by `patient_id`).
2.  **Lab Processing**: Samples are collected and processed by a lab, generating results.
3.  **Result Ingestion**: The lab results are ingested into the system, creating new documents in this collection with `result_value`, `unit`, `reference_range`, `test_name`, `tested_at`, and an initial `status`.
4.  **Doctor Review**: Doctors can access a patient's historical and recent lab results from this collection to assess health status, confirm diagnoses, adjust treatments, and monitor progress. The `status` field indicates readiness for review, and `reference_range` helps in quick interpretation.
5.  **Patient Access**: Patients might access their own lab results, often through a patient portal, to understand their health metrics.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Doctor-Patient Link Requests

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to manage and track requests for establishing a digital connection or relationship between a doctor and a patient within the healthcare system. It facilitates the workflow of requesting, approving, or rejecting these linking attempts, ensuring that appropriate consent and record-keeping are maintained before a secure doctor-patient relationship is established.

KEY_ENTITIES: Each document primarily stores a **Doctor-Patient Link Request**. It is not storing patient or doctor entities themselves, but rather the transactional records of attempts to connect them.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: Unique identifier for this specific link request.
*   `doctor_id`: The unique identifier for the doctor involved in this link request.
*   `patient_user_id`: The unique identifier for the patient's user account involved in this link request.
*   `linked_patient_id`: The unique identifier for the specific patient record/profile that is being linked. This might differ from `patient_user_id` if a user account can manage multiple patient profiles.
*   `patient_name`: Denormalized field storing the patient's name for easy display and context without needing an immediate join to the patient collection.
*   `status`: The current state of the link request (e.g., 'pending', 'approved', 'rejected').
*   `created_at`: Timestamp indicating when the link request was initiated.
*   `resolved_at`: Timestamp indicating when the link request was finalized (approved or rejected).

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Doctors Collection**: `doctor_id` likely refers to an `_id` in a `doctors` or `users` collection (where users can have a doctor role).
*   **Patients/Users Collection**: `patient_user_id` likely refers to an `_id` in a `users` or `patients` collection.
*   **Patient Profiles/Records Collection**: `linked_patient_id` likely refers to an `_id` in a `patient_profiles` or `patients` collection, which holds the actual patient's medical data or profile.
*   **Doctor-Patient Relationships Collection**: Upon `status` becoming 'approved', this collection likely triggers the creation or update of a separate `doctor_patient_relationships` or `connections` collection, which persists the active links for ongoing interactions.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a crucial role in the **Doctor-Patient Relationship Establishment Workflow**:
1.  **Request Initiation**: A doctor (or potentially a patient) initiates a request to link their accounts/records. A new document with `status: 'pending'` is created in `linkrequests`.
2.  **Notification & Review**: The other party (patient or doctor) is notified of the pending request.
3.  **Action**: The recipient reviews the request and decides to either `approve` or `reject` it.
4.  **Resolution**: The `status` field in the `linkrequests` document is updated to 'approved' or 'rejected', and `resolved_at` is set.
5.  **Relationship Activation**: If `approved`, the system proceeds to establish the formal digital relationship (e.g., creating an entry in a `doctor_patient_relationships` collection) which then grants the doctor access to relevant patient data or enables secure communication.
This collection effectively serves as the audit trail and state machine for managing these critical linking processes.
