### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Milestone Rewards

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to track and manage individual reward entitlements that patients have earned by achieving specific milestones within a healthcare or wellness program. It maintains the state of each earned reward, from its initial unlock to its eventual claim status. The primary business purpose is to incentivize patient engagement, loyalty, or specific health behaviors through a structured reward system.

KEY_ENTITIES: The primary entity stored in this collection is an **instance of an earned reward** for a specific patient, representing a single achievement and its associated benefit. It implicitly links to `Patients` and `Reward Definitions`.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `patient_id`: The unique identifier for the patient who has earned this specific reward. It acts as a foreign key linking to the `patients` or `users` collection.
*   `milestone_key`: A string identifier representing the type of reward earned (e.g., 'free_consultation', 'medicine_discount', 'health_report'). This key would typically map to a detailed definition of the reward.
*   `unlocked_at`: A timestamp indicating the exact moment when the patient achieved the underlying milestone and consequently earned this reward.
*   `claimed`: A boolean flag that indicates whether the patient has already redeemed or utilized this specific reward (`true`) or if it is still available for use (`false`).

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **`patients` collection**: The `patient_id` field establishes a Many-to-One relationship with the `_id` field in a `patients` (or `users`) collection, meaning many reward instances can belong to one patient.
*   **`milestones` or `reward_definitions` collection**: The `milestone_key` field would typically link to a separate collection (e.g., `milestone_definitions` or `reward_catalog`) that holds the detailed description, value, terms, and conditions for each type of reward. This is a Many-to-One relationship, where many instances can refer to the same reward type definition.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a crucial role in a patient loyalty, engagement, or gamification program.
1.  **Milestone Achievement & Reward Issuance**: When a patient completes an action or reaches a predefined goal (e.g., completes 5 sessions, refers a friend, achieves a health metric), a system process creates a new document in this collection, recording the `milestone_key` and setting `claimed` to `false`, effectively "unlocking" the reward for the `patient_id`.
2.  **Patient Reward View**: Patients can view their list of unlocked rewards through a patient portal or application, using the data from this collection.
3.  **Reward Redemption**: When a patient decides to use an available reward (e.g., applies a discount, books a free consultation), the `claimed` field for that specific reward instance is updated to `true`, preventing future re-use.
4.  **Reporting and Analytics**: This collection provides essential data for analyzing patient engagement with reward programs, tracking redemption rates, and understanding the popularity and impact of various reward types.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: User Notifications & Alerts

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves as a central repository for all system-generated messages, alerts, and reminders intended for specific users within the application. Its primary business purpose is to keep users informed about important events, status changes, and required actions related to their activities (e.g., patient enrollments, appointments, care plan progress, system alerts), thereby enhancing user engagement, operational awareness, and prompting timely actions.

KEY_ENTITIES:
The primary entity stored in this collection is a **Notification**.
Each notification is targeted at a specific **User** (e.g., a healthcare provider, an administrator, or a patient).
Notifications often refer to or are triggered by events related to other core business entities such as **Patients**, **Appointments**, **Care Plans**, **Programs**, or **Enrollments**.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: MongoDB's unique document identifier for each notification.
*   `user_id`: (String/UUID) Identifies the recipient user for whom this notification is intended. This is crucial for retrieving a user's personalized notification feed.
*   `title`: (String) A concise, human-readable summary or headline for the notification.
*   `message`: (String) The detailed content of the notification, providing more context to the user.
*   `category`: (String) A classification of the notification (e.g., 'enrollment', 'appointment', 'alert', 'feedback', 'program', 'careplan'). Useful for filtering and grouping notifications in the UI.
*   `type`: (String) Indicates the severity or nature of the notification (e.g., 'success', 'info', 'warning'). Often used to drive UI presentation like color coding or iconography.
*   `is_read`: (Boolean) A flag indicating whether the user has viewed or acknowledged the notification. Defaults to `false`.
*   `created_at`: (DateTime) Timestamp indicating when the notification was originally generated.
*   `updatedAt`: (DateTime) Timestamp indicating the last time the notification document was updated (e.g., when `is_read` changes).
*   `related_id`: (String/ObjectId, optional) An identifier for the specific business object that this notification pertains to (e.g., a patient ID, an appointment ID, a care plan ID).
*   `related_type`: (String, optional) The type of business object identified by `related_id` (e.g., 'patient', 'appointment', 'enrollment', 'careplan_assignment'). This enables deep linking or retrieval of related entity details.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Users Collection**: Strongly linked via `user_id` to a `users` collection (or potentially `patients`/`doctors` collections), which holds the profile information for the notification recipient.
*   **Patients Collection**: Notifications related to patient activities (e.g., 'New patient enrolled', 'Low adherence alert for Rajesh Kumar') suggest a link via `related_id` (if present) to a `patients` collection.
*   **Appointments Collection**: 'Appointment reminder' notifications indicate a link via `related_id` to an `appointments` collection.
*   **Care Plans/Programs/Enrollments Collections**: Notifications related to 'careplan', 'program', or 'enrollment' categories often have `related_id` and `related_type` fields pointing to respective `careplans`, `programs`, or `enrollments` collections. This allows for detailed context when a user clicks on a notification.

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection is integral to several real-world workflows, primarily acting as a user communication and engagement layer:
1.  **Provider Workflow (e.g., Doctors/Nurses/Care Managers)**: Informs providers about new patient enrollments, critical patient alerts (e.g., 'Low adherence'), upcoming patient appointments, or feedback requests, enabling them to prioritize tasks and intervene proactively.
2.  **Patient Workflow**: Provides patients with important updates such as appointment reminders, care plan welcome messages, program completion notifications, or feedback requests post-service, keeping them engaged and informed about their health journey.
3.  **System Monitoring & Alerts**: Acts as an alerting mechanism for critical system events or status changes that require user attention.
4.  **Actionable Information Delivery**: Many notifications are designed to prompt specific actions, such as "Start logging today!" for a care plan, "Share your feedback" after an appointment, or "Follow-up with..." for an appointment reminder.
5.  **Historical Record**: Provides a chronological history of important events and communications delivered to a user, which can be reviewed for auditing or context-setting.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient-Doctor Relationship Records

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: To establish, track, and manage the explicit linkages and professional relationships between individual patients and doctors within a healthcare system. This collection serves as a registry for approved connections, enabling controlled access and facilitating secure communication and care coordination.

KEY_ENTITIES: The primary entity stored in this collection is the **Patient-Doctor Link** or **Relationship Record**. This document represents a singular connection instance between one patient and one doctor. Patients and Doctors themselves are distinct entities, referenced here by their unique identifiers.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `patient_user_id`: A unique identifier (UUID) for the patient. This acts as a foreign key to a `patients` or `users` collection, allowing retrieval of full patient details.
*   `doctor_user_id`: A unique identifier (UUID) for the doctor. This acts as a foreign key to a `doctors` or `users` collection, allowing retrieval of full doctor profiles.
*   `status`: A critical field indicating the current state of the relationship (e.g., `requested`, `pending`, `approved`, `active`, `rejected`, `inactive`). This governs permissions and access rights.
*   `requested_at`: A timestamp indicating when the patient (or a system on their behalf) initiated the request to establish this link.
*   `responded_at`: A timestamp indicating when the doctor processed the link request (approved or rejected it).
*   `doctor_name`: (Denormalized) The name of the doctor, likely included for quick display in user interfaces without needing to query the `doctors` collection directly.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Patients Collection:** `patient_user_id` links to a `patients` (or a `users` collection with patient profiles) where comprehensive patient demographics, contact information, and potentially medical history summaries are stored.
*   **Doctors Collection:** `doctor_user_id` links to a `doctors` (or a `users` collection with doctor profiles) where doctor credentials, specializations, contact details, and other professional information reside.
*   **Medical Records / Appointments / Prescriptions Collections:** This collection acts as an authorization layer. Only doctors with an `approved` or `active` link to a patient, as recorded here, would typically be granted access to that patient's `medical_records`, allowed to schedule `appointments`, or issue `prescriptions` for them.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection is fundamental to managing the lifecycle of patient-doctor engagements:
1.  **Link Request Initiation:** A patient (or their authorized representative) initiates a request to link with a specific doctor. A new document is created with a `pending` or `requested` status.
2.  **Doctor Review and Action:** The designated doctor receives notification of the pending request. They review it and can either `approve` or `reject` the link. The `status` and `responded_at` fields are updated accordingly.
3.  **Access and Authorization:** Upon `approval` or becoming `active`, this record grants the linked doctor specific permissions, such as the ability to view the patient's medical history, initiate secure communication, or manage their treatment plan.
4.  **Relationship Monitoring:** It provides an ongoing record of active relationships, crucial for continuity of care, communication, billing, and compliance auditing.
5.  **Relationship Termination:** If a patient or doctor decides to end the relationship, the `status` can be updated (e.g., to `inactive` or `terminated`), which subsequently revokes the doctor's access privileges to that patient's data.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Medical Document Insights

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves as a central repository for digitized patient medical documents (like prescriptions, lab reports, imaging results) and, critically, stores the AI-extracted, summarized, and structured insights derived from these documents. Its primary purpose is to transform unstructured medical data into easily accessible and actionable information for patients and healthcare providers.

KEY_ENTITIES:
The primary entity stored in this collection is a **Processed Medical Document Record**. Each record encapsulates the original document's metadata, its digital content (via `file_path`), and the extensive AI-generated analysis.
It implicitly references **Patients** (via `patient_id`) and **Doctors** (via `doctor_id`, `uploaded_by`).

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: Unique identifier for the processed document record.
*   `patient_id`: Foreign key linking to the patient's primary record in a `patients` collection. Essential for retrieving all documents related to a specific patient.
*   `doctor_id`: Foreign key linking to the doctor associated with the content of the document (e.g., the prescribing doctor, or the doctor who authored a report).
*   `uploaded_by`: ID of the user (likely a doctor or administrative staff) who uploaded the original file, potentially linking to a `users` or `doctors` collection.
*   `file_name`, `file_path`, `file_type`, `file_size_bytes`: Metadata pointing to the original uploaded document file, allowing retrieval of the source.
*   `ai_summary`: A professional, AI-generated summary of the document's clinical content, intended for healthcare professionals.
*   `layman_summary`: A simplified, AI-generated summary of the document's content, intended for patient consumption.
*   `extracted_data`: The core structured data extracted by the AI, which can include `key_points` and a detailed `medications` array (for prescriptions), providing actionable information.
*   `category`: A classification of the document type (e.g., 'general', 'prescription', 'report').
*   `analyzed_at`: Timestamp indicating when the AI processing and data extraction occurred.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **`patients` collection**: A many-to-one relationship via `patient_id`. Many documents can belong to one patient.
*   **`doctors` collection**: A many-to-one relationship via `doctor_id`. Many documents can be associated with one doctor.
*   **`users` or `doctors` collection**: A many-to-one relationship via `uploaded_by`. Many documents can be uploaded by one user/doctor. (Note: `doctor_id` and `uploaded_by` may point to the same or different entities depending on system design).
*   Potentially, a **`medications` or `drug_master` collection**: If the `extracted_data.medications.medicine` field links to a canonical drug reference for drug interaction checks, dosage information, etc.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a pivotal role in a digital health ecosystem by supporting several key workflows:
1.  **Document Digitization and Intelligent Archiving**: Serves as the destination for uploaded patient documents, transforming raw files into structured, searchable records.
2.  **Clinical Decision Support**: Healthcare providers can rapidly access AI-generated summaries and extracted data from various documents, enabling quicker diagnoses and treatment planning without sifting through original, lengthy records.
3.  **Patient Engagement and Education**: Layman summaries empower patients to understand their medical reports and prescriptions, fostering better adherence and self-management.
4.  **Automated Medication Management**: For prescriptions, the structured `extracted_data.medications` can feed into systems for automated refill requests, medication reminders, and drug interaction alerts.
5.  **Historical Record Keeping**: Provides a chronologically ordered, searchable history of a patient's health journey through all their medical documents.
6.  **Audit and Compliance**: The timestamps and `uploaded_by` fields support auditing capabilities, crucial for regulatory compliance in healthcare.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Gamification Profiles

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to store and manage the gamification progress and aggregated health-tracking metrics for individual patients. Its primary business purpose is to motivate patient engagement and adherence to health management programs by providing a system of points, levels, and streaks based on their logging activities. It offers a snapshot of a patient's overall participation and achievements within the gamified health application.

KEY_ENTITIES: The primary entity stored in this collection is a **Patient's Gamification Profile / Progress**. Each document uniquely represents the current gamification status and aggregated logging statistics for a single patient.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: (ObjectId) The unique identifier for this gamification profile document.
*   `patient_id`: (String) A foreign key linking this document to the specific patient in a `patients` or `users` collection. Essential for identifying whose gamification profile this is.
*   `level`: (Number) The patient's current gamification level, indicating their overall progress.
*   `level_label`: (String) A human-readable description of the current `level` (e.g., "Beginner", "Consistent").
*   `total_points`: (Number) The cumulative sum of all points earned by the patient across all health logging activities.
*   `current_streak`: (Number) The number of consecutive days the patient has performed at least one health logging activity.
*   `longest_streak`: (Number) The maximum number of consecutive logging days achieved by the patient.
*   `last_log_date`: (String/Date) The date of the most recent health activity logged by the patient, crucial for streak calculation.
*   `bp_logs`, `food_logs`, `medication_logs`, `sugar_logs`: (Numbers) Aggregated counts of the specific types of health data logs submitted by the patient. These reflect the patient's activity volume for each category.
*   `points_bp`, `points_food`, `points_medication`, `points_sugar`: (Numbers) The points earned specifically for logging each type of health data.
*   `health_score`: (Number) An overall calculated score that might reflect a broader measure of health behavior or compliance (though 0 in samples, implying it might be a future feature or calculated externally).
*   `created_at`: (Datetime) Timestamp when this gamification profile was first created for the patient.
*   `updated_at`: (Datetime) Timestamp of the last time this gamification profile was updated, typically when new logs are added or streaks/points are recalculated.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **`patients` (or `users`) collection**: The `patient_id` field forms a direct relationship with a `patients` collection, where core patient demographic and personal information would be stored. This is a one-to-one relationship (one gamification profile per patient).
*   **Specific Log Collections (e.g., `bloodpressurelogs`, `foodentries`, `medicationadherence`, `bloodsugarreadings`)**: This collection is likely updated *from* more granular log collections. When a patient submits a new blood pressure reading, an entry is added to `bloodpressurelogs`, and then this `patientgamifications` document is updated to increment `bp_logs` and `points_bp`. This implies a many-to-one relationship (many log entries contribute to one gamification profile).
*   **`rewards` or `achievements` collection (potential)**: Could be linked if reaching certain levels, points, or streaks unlocks specific rewards, badges, or achievements stored in a separate collection.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection is integral to the gamification layer of a health application.
1.  **Patient Dashboard Display**: It enables the application to quickly retrieve and display a patient's current gamification status (level, points, streaks) on their personal dashboard, providing instant feedback and motivation.
2.  **Engagement Loop**: After a patient logs a health activity (e.g., blood pressure, food intake), the system updates this collection, recalculating points, streaks, and potentially levels. This immediate update reinforces positive behavior.
3.  **Progress Tracking**: It allows patients (and potentially their care providers) to track their long-term engagement and adherence patterns through historical streaks and accumulated points.
4.  **Gamification Engine Output**: It serves as the persistent storage for the output of the gamification engine, which processes individual patient actions and translates them into gamified metrics.
5.  **Targeted Interventions**: The aggregated data (e.g., low `total_logs` or `current_streak`) could trigger alerts or prompts to re-engage patients who are showing reduced activity.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Health Profiles and Engagement Data

COLLECTION_PURPOSE:
This collection serves as the central repository for individual patient profiles within a healthcare or wellness management system. Its primary purpose is to store and manage comprehensive patient demographic information, core health data (conditions, medications), contact details, and system-level tracking related to patient engagement and communication, enabling effective patient management, care coordination, and automated outreach.

KEY_ENTITIES:
The primary entity stored in this collection is a **Patient**.
There are foreign key references to other entities like **Doctor** (via `doctor_id`) and **Clinic** (via `clinic_id`), indicating that these entities are managed in separate, related collections. Some documents also indicate a potential **User** entity if patients have direct access accounts (via `patient_user_id`).

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each patient document.
*   `full_name`: The patient's full name, essential for identification.
*   `age`, `gender`: Basic demographic information.
*   `phone`, `emergency_contact`: Critical contact information for communication and emergencies.
*   `conditions`: An array listing the patient's diagnosed medical conditions.
*   `medications`: An array listing the patient's current prescribed medications.
*   `status`: Indicates the patient's current state or engagement level in the system (e.g., 'active', 'at_risk'), which can drive system logic or interventions.
*   `doctor_id`: A foreign key linking the patient to their assigned doctor or care provider.
*   `clinic_id`: A foreign key linking the patient to the clinic or healthcare facility they belong to.
*   `patient_user_id`: (When present) A unique identifier linking this patient record to a specific user account, likely for patient portal access or app interaction.
*   `last_food_log_reminder_date`, `last_tip_sent_date`, `last_workout_tip_sent_date`: Timestamps indicating the last time automated reminders or health tips were sent, crucial for managing patient engagement and preventing over-communication.
*   `reminders_sent_today`: A nested document tracking daily reminder activities, specifically for medicines.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **One-to-Many with Doctors:** The `doctor_id` field establishes a relationship with a `doctors` (or `users`) collection, where one doctor can be associated with multiple patients.
*   **One-to-Many with Clinics:** The `clinic_id` field establishes a relationship with a `clinics` collection, where one clinic can have multiple patients.
*   **One-to-One (Optional) with Users:** The `patient_user_id` (when present) likely links to a `users` or `accounts` collection if patients have their own login accounts for a patient portal or mobile application.
*   **Referenced by other collections:** This `patients` collection is likely referenced by many other collections that store patient-specific data, such as `appointments` (linking to patient `_id`), `health_logs` (e.g., food, activity, vitals, each entry linking to patient `_id`), `treatment_plans` (linking to patient `_id`), or `messages` (for communication history).

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection plays a critical role in several real-world workflows:
1.  **Patient Onboarding & Registration:** It's the primary destination for creating new patient records, capturing initial demographics and health information upon registration.
2.  **Patient Management & Care Planning:** Healthcare providers and administrative staff use this data to view, update, and manage patient profiles, understand their conditions and medications, and support the development of care plans.
3.  **Automated Patient Engagement:** The reminder and tip tracking fields (`last_food_log_reminder_date`, `last_tip_sent_date`, etc.) facilitate automated systems for sending health reminders, personalized tips (e.g., for diet or exercise), and medication adherence notifications, promoting proactive health management.
4.  **Care Coordination:** By linking patients to specific doctors and clinics, it enables efficient assignment and management of patients within a healthcare ecosystem.
5.  **Clinical Decision Support:** The `conditions` and `medications` arrays provide quick access to vital health information, aiding doctors in making informed clinical decisions.
6.  **Reporting and Analytics:** The structured patient data forms the basis for various operational and analytical reports, such as patient demographics analysis, disease prevalence tracking, and engagement metrics.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Access Vault Codes

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to securely store and manage unique, time-bound or revocable access codes (vault codes) assigned to individual patients. These codes are used to grant specific patients authorized access to certain data, features, or services within a healthcare platform. It tracks the ownership, status, and lifecycle of each code.

KEY_ENTITIES: The primary entity represented in this collection is a **Patient Vault Code Assignment**. Each document signifies that a specific `vault_code` has been issued to a particular `patient_user_id`. Therefore, it stores instances of vault codes and their direct association with patients.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `patient_user_id`: A unique identifier (likely a UUID) linking this vault code to a specific patient's profile in a separate collection. This is crucial for identifying who the code belongs to.
*   `vault_code`: The actual unique, alphanumeric code generated for patient access. This is the core data element.
*   `is_active`: A boolean flag indicating whether the vault code is currently valid and usable. This is essential for controlling access and revoking codes.
*   `created_at`: Timestamp indicating when the vault code was initially generated and assigned. Useful for auditing and potential expiration policies.
*   `updatedAt`: Timestamp indicating the last modification to the vault code's record (e.g., activation/deactivation).

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Patients/Users Collection**: Directly relates via `patient_user_id` which acts as a foreign key, referencing the `_id` (or similar unique identifier) of a patient's record in a `patients` or `users` collection. This establishes who each vault code belongs to.
*   **Service/Data Access Modules**: Indirectly related to other modules or collections that *consume* these vault codes for authentication or authorization. For example, a "Patient Portal" module might validate a vault code against this collection before granting access to patient records.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection supports real-world workflows centered around secure patient access and controlled data sharing. Examples include:
1.  **Patient Portal Login/Authentication**: A patient might receive a temporary vault code to log into a secure patient portal, acting as a single-use password or part of a multi-factor authentication process.
2.  **Secure Document Viewing**: A patient uses a vault code to unlock and view sensitive medical records, test results, or consent forms, ensuring that only the authorized patient (or someone they share the code with) can access the information.
3.  **Third-Party Data Sharing**: A patient or physician generates a vault code to grant temporary, limited access to specific patient data to a third party (e.g., another specialist, insurance provider) for a defined period or purpose.
4.  **Service Redemption**: A patient uses a vault code to redeem a particular service, appointment, or benefit that has been pre-authorized.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: User Profiles

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves as a central repository for basic profile information of all users within the system, differentiating between patients and doctors. Its primary goal is to provide essential identity details, contact information, and specific attributes (like medical specialties for doctors) required for various application functionalities, such as user display, search, and linking to other transactional data.

KEY_ENTITIES:
This collection stores **Users**, specifically distinguishing between:
*   **Patients**: Individuals receiving medical services (identified by the absence of `doctor_code` and typically empty `specialties`).
*   **Doctors**: Medical professionals providing services (identified by the presence of `doctor_code` and potentially populated `specialties`).

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: MongoDB's unique document identifier.
*   `user_id`: A UUID (Universally Unique Identifier) that acts as an external foreign key, likely linking to a core `users` or `authentication` collection where login credentials and basic user accounts are managed. This is the primary identifier for a user across the system.
*   `full_name`: The complete name of the user, whether a patient or a doctor. Used for display and search.
*   `doctor_code`: An optional, unique identifier for doctors. Its presence distinguishes a doctor profile from a patient profile. It might be used for internal identification or linking to external doctor directories.
*   `specialties`: An array of strings listing the medical specializations of a doctor (e.g., "General Medicine", "Diabetology"). This field is crucial for doctor search and filtering, and typically empty for patient profiles.
*   `phone`: The contact phone number of the user. Used for communication purposes.
*   `createdAt`: Timestamp indicating when the profile was first created.
*   `updatedAt`: Timestamp indicating when the profile was last modified.

RELATIONSHIPS:
This `profiles` collection likely serves as a foundational "identity" collection and connects to many other collections:
*   **`users` (or `auth`) collection**: Via `user_id`, for authentication, authorization, and core user account management.
*   **`appointments` collection**: Both patients and doctors would be referenced by their `user_id` in appointment records (e.g., `patient_id`, `doctor_id`).
*   **`medical_records` (or `patient_history`) collection**: Patient profiles (via `user_id`) would be linked to their medical history.
*   **`reviews` collection**: Users (both patients reviewing doctors, and potentially doctors reviewing patients) would be linked via `user_id`.
*   **`clinics` or `hospitals` collection**: Doctors (via `doctor_code` or `user_id`) might be associated with specific clinics or hospital affiliations.
*   **`billing` or `payments` collection**: User profiles (via `user_id`) would be linked for financial transactions.

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection plays a critical role in several real-world workflows:
1.  **User Registration & Onboarding**: When a new patient or doctor registers, their basic profile information is stored here.
2.  **Profile Management**: Users (both patients and doctors) can view and update their personal details, contact information, and doctors can update their specialties.
3.  **Doctor Search & Discovery**: Patients can search for doctors based on name, specialty, or location, relying on `full_name` and `specialties` fields.
4.  **Appointment Booking**: When an appointment is scheduled, the `profiles` collection is used to retrieve and display patient and doctor details.
5.  **User Interface Display**: Displaying user names, contact info, and doctor specialties across the application (e.g., patient dashboard, doctor profiles, appointment confirmations).
6.  **Access Control & Personalization**: Differentiating between doctor and patient profiles (via `doctor_code` presence) allows the system to apply role-specific functionalities and views.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE:
Healthcare Program Templates

COLLECTION_PURPOSE:
This collection serves to define and store the blueprints or templates for various standardized medical and care programs that can be offered to patients. It allows for the creation, management, and categorization of different types of care plans, ensuring consistency and structured delivery of healthcare services by doctors.

KEY_ENTITIES:
The primary entity stored here is a "Program" or "Care Plan Template". Each document represents a predefined program that outlines a specific type of care, its duration, and associated details.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: Unique identifier for each program template.
*   `name`: A concise, human-readable name for the program (e.g., "NCD Management").
*   `description`: A more detailed explanation of what the program entails.
*   `type`: Categorization of the program (e.g., 'ncd' for Non-Communicable Disease, 'post_discharge' for post-hospital care, 'elder_care'). Useful for filtering and grouping programs.
*   `duration_days`: The intended duration of the program in days.
*   `is_active`: A boolean flag indicating whether the program template is currently active and available for use.
*   `doctor_id`: A reference to the doctor who created, owns, or is primarily associated with this program template. This suggests ownership or specialized programs by particular practitioners.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Doctors Collection**: The `doctor_id` field links this collection to a `doctors` (or `users` with a doctor role) collection. This indicates which doctor is responsible for or offers this particular program template.
*   **PatientPrograms/Enrollments Collection**: This collection acts as a master list of available programs. Individual patients would be "enrolled" into instances of these programs. Therefore, it would likely connect to a `patient_programs` or `enrollments` collection, which would store patient-specific details, start/end dates, progress, and reference a `program_id` from this collection.
*   **Services/Activities Collection (Potential)**: A program might comprise specific services, consultations, or activities. There could be a separate collection for `services` or `activities` that links back to `program_id` to define the components of each program.

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection plays a central role in the following workflows:
1.  **Program Definition & Management**: Allows doctors or clinic administrators to define, standardize, categorize, and maintain a catalog of available healthcare programs.
2.  **Patient Care Planning**: Serves as a library from which doctors can select and assign appropriate care plans to patients based on their needs (e.g., enrolling a patient in "NCD Management").
3.  **Service Offerings**: Forms the basis of service offerings presented to patients or for internal operational planning, ensuring consistency in the care provided across different patients for similar conditions.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: User Interaction Sessions

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to track and manage ongoing interactive sessions with users, primarily for a conversational AI or chatbot system. It stores the current state and contextual data for each user's interaction, enabling the system to maintain conversational flow, remember user context, and personalize responses across multiple interactions.

KEY_ENTITIES: The primary entity stored here is a **User Session** or **Conversation Session**. Each document represents an active or recently active dialogue thread with a specific user.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each session document, automatically generated by MongoDB.
*   `created_at`: A timestamp indicating when this specific session was first initiated.
*   `updated_at`: A timestamp indicating the last time this session's data was modified, reflecting recent user activity or system updates to the session.
*   `phone`: The phone number of the user involved in this session. This acts as a unique identifier for the user within the system and is crucial for linking sessions to specific users.
*   `state`: Represents the current phase or state of the conversation or interaction for this user (e.g., 'main_menu', 'awaiting_input', 'meal_logging'). This field is fundamental for controlling the conversational flow.
*   `data`: A flexible document field used to store dynamic, session-specific context. This can include:
    *   `last_bot_message`: The last message sent by the bot, useful for displaying conversation history or for context-aware responses.
    *   Other temporary variables or data points relevant to the current interaction, such as partially collected information, user preferences for the current session, or results of recent operations (e.g., meal analysis output).

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Users/Customers Collection (via `phone`):** The `phone` field strongly implies a connection to a `users` or `customers` collection, which would hold permanent user profile information such as names, registration details, long-term preferences, and historical data about the user beyond just the current session.
*   **Interaction Logs/History Collection (implicit):** While `sessions` stores the current state and last message, a more comprehensive `logs` or `history` collection might store a detailed chronological record of *all* messages exchanged within a session for auditing, analytics, or debugging.
*   **Meal Data/Nutrition Collection (via `data` content):** The example `data` field showing "Meal Analysis" suggests a potential link to a `meal_data` or `nutrition_database` collection that the bot queries or updates when users log meals.
*   **Bot/Service Configuration Collection (implicit):** The `state` and `data` fields are interpreted by a specific bot or service logic. There might be a `bots` or `services` collection defining the available conversational flows, responses, and integration points.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection is central to the operation of a conversational AI or chatbot. It supports the following workflow:
1.  **Incoming Message Handling:** When a user sends a message (e.g., via WhatsApp, SMS), the system retrieves the corresponding session document using the user's `phone` number.
2.  **Context Retrieval:** It provides the current `state` of the conversation and any relevant `data` (e.g., `last_bot_message`, partial inputs) from the previous interaction.
3.  **Stateful Processing:** The bot uses the `state` and `data` to correctly interpret the incoming message, determine the appropriate response, and advance the conversation. For example, if `state` is 'meal_logging_awaiting_image', an incoming image would be processed as a meal input.
4.  **Session Update:** After processing, the session document is updated with the new `state`, `data` (e.g., the bot's new message, updated context), and `updated_at` timestamp.
5.  **Session Persistence:** This allows users to pause and resume conversations without losing context, providing a seamless user experience. It acts as the memory for the ongoing dialogue between the user and the system.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: User Role Registry

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to define and manage the functional roles assigned to individual users within the system. It enables role-based access control, allowing the application to differentiate user permissions, features, and data access based on their assigned role (e.g., doctor, patient, clinic).

KEY_ENTITIES:
Each document in this collection represents a **User-Role Assignment**. The primary entities stored are:
*   **Users**: Referenced by `user_id`.
*   **Roles**: Defined by the `role` field.
*   **Clinics/Organizations**: Referenced by `clinic_id` for specific roles, indicating an association with an organizational entity.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id` (ObjectId): The unique identifier for this specific user-role assignment document.
*   `user_id` (String - UUID): A unique identifier that links this role assignment to a specific user. This acts as a foreign key to a `users` or `accounts` collection where detailed user information is stored.
*   `role` (String): Specifies the functional role assigned to the user. Examples observed include 'doctor', 'patient', and 'clinic'. This field is critical for determining a user's permissions and capabilities within the application.
*   `clinic_id` (String - ObjectId, conditional): Present only when the `role` is 'clinic'. This field provides a unique identifier for a specific clinic or organization, likely linking to a `clinics` or `organizations` collection. It indicates that the `user_id` associated with this document is acting *as* or *for* this particular clinic entity.
*   `__v` (Number): A version key, commonly used by Mongoose in Node.js applications, for optimistic locking.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Users/Accounts Collection:** This collection has a strong relationship with a primary `users` or `accounts` collection (not shown). The `user_id` field acts as a foreign key, linking each role assignment to a specific user's profile and authentication details.
*   **Clinics/Organizations Collection:** For roles like 'clinic', the `clinic_id` field establishes a relationship with a `clinics` or `organizations` collection (not shown), providing details about the associated organizational entity.
*   **Authorization/Permissions System:** This collection is foundational for any Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) system. The `role` field directly informs what granular permissions a user possesses, which is typically interpreted by a separate authorization module.

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection plays a crucial role in several core application workflows:
*   **User Onboarding and Registration:** Assigning an initial default role (e.g., 'patient' upon self-registration) or a verified role (e.g., 'doctor' or 'clinic' after approval) to new users.
*   **Authentication and Authorization:** Upon user login, the assigned `role` is retrieved to determine what application features, data, and sections the user is authorized to view or interact with.
*   **User Management:** Administrators or support staff can modify existing user roles, granting or revoking access to different parts of the system.
*   **Application Customization:** The application's user interface, available functionalities, and business logic can be dynamically tailored based on the logged-in user's role, providing a personalized experience.
*   **Multi-tenancy Support:** For 'clinic' roles, it helps differentiate users who operate on behalf of an organization, enabling segregation of data and functionality specific to that clinic.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Weekly Challenge Progress Records

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to track and record the specific weekly health challenges undertaken and completed by individual patients, including completion timestamps and awarded rewards. It acts as a history and current state tracker for patient engagement with gamified health initiatives.

KEY_ENTITIES:
The primary entity represented by each document is a **Patient's Weekly Challenge Completion Record**.
It implicitly links to two other key entities:
*   **Patient**: Identified by `patient_id`.
*   **Challenge Definition**: Identified by `challenge_key`.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for this specific challenge completion record.
*   `patient_id`: A reference to the unique identifier of the patient who participated in the challenge. This is crucial for associating challenge activity with a specific user.
*   `challenge_key`: A unique identifier or slug for the specific challenge (e.g., 'sugar_5_days'). This key would typically link to a separate collection that defines the challenge's details, rules, and goals.
*   `week_start`: The start date of the week during which this challenge was active or assigned. This helps delineate weekly cycles for recurring challenges.
*   `completed_at`: A timestamp indicating when the patient successfully completed the challenge. This is vital for tracking progress and for any time-based reward or reporting logic.
*   `reward_points_awarded`: The number of points or other rewards granted to the patient upon successful completion of this challenge, supporting gamification features.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **`patients` or `users` collection**: The `patient_id` field forms a direct relationship (many-to-one) to the `_id` of a document in a `patients` or `users` collection, which stores detailed information about each patient/user.
*   **`challenges` or `challenge_definitions` collection**: The `challenge_key` field likely refers to a `key` or `_id` in a separate `challenges` collection. This collection would store the static definitions, descriptions, rules, and potential rewards for each type of challenge.

WORKFLOW_ROLE:
This collection plays a critical role in supporting workflows related to:
1.  **Patient Engagement & Gamification**: It records patient participation and successful completion of health challenges, driving user engagement through a reward system.
2.  **Progress Tracking**: It allows the system, patients, and potentially care providers to monitor a patient's adherence to and completion of assigned weekly health goals over time.
3.  **Reward Management**: It facilitates the automatic awarding and tracking of reward points when a patient achieves a challenge objective.
4.  **Personalized Health Journeys**: Provides data to tailor future challenge recommendations or interventions based on a patient's historical engagement and success.
5.  **Reporting & Analytics**: Serves as a primary data source for reporting on patient engagement rates, challenge popularity, completion rates, and the impact of gamification strategies.

### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: Patient Vital Signs Records

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves the business purpose of storing and managing individual vital sign measurements for patients within a healthcare system. It enables tracking patient health over time, supporting medical diagnosis, treatment planning, and monitoring patient conditions by providing a historical record of key physiological data.

KEY_ENTITIES: The primary entity stored here is an individual **Vital Measurement** event. Each document represents a single recording of a specific vital sign (e.g., one blood pressure reading, one heart rate measurement) for a particular patient at a given time, potentially recorded or supervised by a doctor. It implicitly references **Patients** and **Doctors**.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each vital sign record.
*   `patient_id`: A foreign key referencing the `_id` of the patient to whom this vital sign belongs. Essential for linking measurements to specific individuals.
*   `doctor_id`: A foreign key referencing the `_id` of the doctor who recorded or is associated with this vital sign measurement. Useful for auditing and tracking care providers.
*   `vital_type`: Describes the type of vital sign being recorded (e.g., 'blood_pressure', 'heart_rate', 'temperature', 'weight'). Critical for categorizing and interpreting the data.
*   `value_numeric`: The numerical value of the vital sign. Used for calculations, graphing, and threshold checks.
*   `value_text`: A text representation of the vital sign, often useful for values that have a standard string format (e.g., '120/80' for blood pressure) or for displaying purposes.
*   `unit`: The unit of measurement for the vital sign (e.g., 'bpm', '°F', 'kg'). Ensures correct interpretation of `value_numeric`.
*   `recorded_at`: The timestamp indicating when the vital sign was actually measured or taken. Crucial for chronological tracking and analysis.
*   `created_at`, `updatedAt`: Standard metadata timestamps tracking when the record was first created and last modified in the database.

RELATIONSHIPS: This collection has a clear relationship with other collections, primarily:
*   **Patients Collection**: Each vital sign record is linked to a specific patient via the `patient_id` field. This is a one-to-many relationship (one patient can have many vital records).
*   **Doctors Collection**: Each vital sign record can be linked to a specific doctor via the `doctor_id` field. This is also a one-to-many relationship (one doctor can record many vital signs).
These relationships are typically established through foreign keys (`patient_id`, `doctor_id`) pointing to the `_id` fields in their respective master collections.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection supports core clinical and administrative workflows in a healthcare setting, including:
1.  **Patient Monitoring**: Doctors and nurses regularly record new vital signs, which are then stored here.
2.  **Clinical Review**: Clinicians can retrieve and review a patient's historical vital signs to assess trends, evaluate treatment effectiveness, and make informed medical decisions.
3.  **Alerting Systems**: Automated systems can query this collection to detect vital signs falling outside normal ranges and trigger alerts for medical staff.
4.  **Health Analytics**: Data from this collection can be aggregated and analyzed for population health management, research, and identifying common health patterns or risks.
5.  **Electronic Health Records (EHR) Display**: This data is crucial for populating the vital signs section of a patient's EHR interface, providing a comprehensive view of their physiological state.

               'timestamp': datetime.datetime(2026, 2, 20, 10, 25, 43, 806000)},
              {'_id': ObjectId('699836a7169a4b93d2ac53de'),
               'content': "You're welcome, Bhuvan. Just remember to prioritize your sleep and try to have regular, balanced meals. If you "
                          'ever have any concerns or questions, feel free to reach out. Take care and have a wonderful day!',
               'role': 'assistant',
               'timestamp': datetime.datetime(2026, 2, 20, 10, 25, 43, 806000)}],
 'patient_id': '69982a4c169a4b93d2ac51c3',
 'session_date': datetime.datetime(2026, 2, 20, 10, 25, 43, 806000),
 'updatedAt': datetime.datetime(2026, 2, 20, 10, 25, 43, 810000)}


### COLLECTION INTELLIGENCE SUMMARY ###
COLLECTION_TITLE: AI Health Conversation Records

COLLECTION_PURPOSE: This collection serves to store the complete history and metadata of interactions between patients and an AI-powered health companion (represented by a "doctor persona"). Its primary business purpose is to enable the tracking, analysis, and continuous improvement of the AI's performance, understand patient engagement, and provide a comprehensive record of virtual health check-ins or consultations.

KEY_ENTITIES:
*   **Conversation/Session**: The primary entity, representing a single continuous dialogue exchange between a patient and the AI. Each document is a conversation session.
*   **Patient**: Referenced by `patient_id`. This is the human user engaging with the AI health companion.
*   **AI Doctor Persona**: Referenced by `doctor_persona`. This represents the specific AI personality or model that interacted with the patient.
*   **Message**: An embedded entity within a conversation, representing an individual turn or utterance in the dialogue, exchanged between the user and the assistant.

IMPORTANT_FIELDS:
*   `_id`: The unique identifier for each voice conversation session, crucial for referencing and retrieval.
*   `patient_id`: A foreign key linking this conversation to a specific patient profile, essential for maintaining patient history and personalization.
*   `doctor_persona`: Identifies the specific AI model or persona engaged in the conversation, allowing for tracking AI variant performance and persona-specific analysis.
*   `messages`: An embedded array containing the full transcript of the conversation, including the content, speaker role (`user` or `assistant`), and timestamp of each individual message. This is the core content of the interaction.
*   `duration_seconds`: The total length of the conversation, useful for engagement metrics and resource allocation analysis.
*   `session_date`: The timestamp indicating when the conversation session began, critical for chronological analysis and historical reporting.
*   `extracted_actions`: (Though empty in samples, its presence is significant) This field is designed to store structured information about specific actions, recommendations, or identified needs from the conversation (e.g., "remind patient to take medication," "suggest a healthy recipe"). It's vital for driving actionable insights and integrating with other healthcare processes.

RELATIONSHIPS:
*   **Patients Collection**: The `patient_id` field strongly links to a separate `patients` (or `users`) collection, which would hold detailed demographic information, medical history, preferences, and other master data about each patient.
*   **AI Personas/Models Collection**: The `doctor_persona` field likely refers to a `ai_personas` or `ai_models` collection that defines the configuration, characteristics, and possibly versioning of different AI health companions.
*   **Analytics & Reporting Systems**: Data from `voiceconversations` (e.g., duration, message content for sentiment analysis, extracted actions) would feed into dedicated analytics platforms or `reports` collections for performance monitoring, business intelligence, and AI model evaluation.
*   **Care Plan / Intervention Collections**: If `extracted_actions` lead to concrete healthcare interventions or personalized care plans, this collection would have an implicit or explicit relationship with collections managing such plans.

WORKFLOW_ROLE: This collection plays a central role in supporting the **lifecycle of an AI-powered virtual health assistant service**.
1.  **Patient Engagement Logging**: It serves as the authoritative record for every interaction a patient has with the AI, forming a digital history of their engagement.
2.  **AI Performance Monitoring & Improvement**: Developers and product teams use this data to evaluate the AI's conversational quality, accuracy, empathy, and adherence to protocols. Transcripts facilitate debugging and identifying areas for AI model retraining.
3.  **Personalized Patient Support**: The historical conversation data can be leveraged by the AI itself (or human caregivers) to provide more context-aware and personalized support in future interactions.
4.  **Auditing and Compliance**: In a healthcare context, these records are crucial for auditing purposes, ensuring compliance with health regulations, and addressing any patient concerns or disputes.
5.  **Feature Development & Research**: The rich dataset of conversations is invaluable for developing new AI capabilities, understanding patient needs, and driving research into conversational AI in healthcare.


########################################################################################################################
########## COMPLETE DATABASE ARCHITECTURE SUMMARY ##########
########################################################################################################################

Mediimate is designed as a comprehensive digital health platform, integrating patient management, care delivery, engagement, and operational oversight. The system leverages a microservices-oriented architecture, where distinct functional domains are supported by dedicated MongoDB collections. This allows for scalability, specialized data handling, and clear separation of concerns, typical of modern cloud-native applications.

The platform's core revolves around managing patient health journeys, from onboarding and personalized care plans to ongoing monitoring, AI-driven interactions, and performance feedback. It caters to multiple user types: patients, doctors, and clinic administrators, providing tailored experiences and controlled access to sensitive health information. AI plays a significant role in document processing (summarizing lab reports and medical documents) and patient interaction (chat/voice assistants).

The system architecture prioritizes:
1.  **Patient-Centricity**: All data and workflows ultimately aim to support the patient's health and engagement.
2.  **Provider Enablement**: Tools for doctors to manage schedules, oversee care plans, and review patient data efficiently.
3.  **Data-Driven Insights**: Extensive logging and tracking enable analytics for patient adherence, program effectiveness, and operational efficiency.
4.  **Security & Compliance**: Structured handling of user authentication, roles, and patient data access (e.g., `patientvaultcodes`, `patientdoctorlinks`).
5.  **Scalability**: A MongoDB foundation allows for flexible schema evolution and horizontal scaling to accommodate a growing user base and data volume.

---

### CORE_DOMAINS

The Mediimate system is structured around several core business modules, each managing a distinct set of functionalities and data:

1.  **User & Identity Management (UIM)**: This domain handles all aspects of user authentication, registration, profiles, and role assignments across the platform. It provides the foundational identity layer for patients, doctors, and administrators.
    *   *Collections*: `authusers`, `profiles`, `userroles`, `clinicinvites`, `clinicmembers`, `patientvaultcodes`

2.  **Patient Data & Health Tracking (PDHT)**: This is the central repository for comprehensive patient health information, including demographics, medical conditions, and various health measurements and documents. It forms the patient's digital health record.
    *   *Collections*: `patients`, `vitals`, `foodlogs`, `labresults`, `labreports`, `patientdocuments`

3.  **Care Planning & Program Management (CPPM)**: This domain defines, assigns, and tracks patient participation and progress within structured health programs and individualized care plans. It's crucial for chronic disease management and wellness initiatives.
    *   *Collections*: `programs`, `careplans`, `enrollments`, `careplanassignments`

4.  **Appointment & Scheduling (AS)**: This module manages the scheduling of appointments, doctor availability, and the real-time tracking of patient visits at clinics. It ensures efficient resource allocation and patient flow.
    *   *Collections*: `appointments`, `appointmentcheckins`, `doctoravailabilities`

5.  **AI & Conversational Health (ACH)**: This domain powers the AI-driven patient interactions, storing chat and voice conversation transcripts and managing the real-time session context for AI assistants.
    *   *Collections*: `chatconversations`, `voiceconversations`, `sessions`

6.  **Notifications & Communications (NC)**: This module handles all system-generated messages, alerts, and audit trails for communication with users, ensuring patients and providers are informed and engaged.
    *   *Collections*: `emailnotificationlogs`, `notifications`, `alerts`

7.  **Patient Engagement & Gamification (PEG)**: This domain focuses on motivating patients through gamified elements like points, levels, streaks, and rewards for adherence to care plans and health logging activities.
    *   *Collections*: `patientgamifications`, `milestonerewards`, `userweeklychallenges`

8.  **Clinic & Provider Management (CPM)**: This module manages the master data for healthcare clinics, doctor-patient relationships, and the process of establishing those connections.
    *   *Collections*: `clinics`, `patientdoctorlinks`, `linkrequests`

9.  **Feedback & Quality Assurance (FQA)**: This domain manages the collection and storage of patient feedback regarding appointments and services, crucial for quality improvement and service evaluation.
    *   *Collections*: `feedbackrequests`, `feedbacks`

10. **Business Development & CRM (BDCRM)**: This module captures and tracks initial inquiries from prospective customers or clinics, supporting lead generation and sales processes.
    *   *Collections*: `contactleads`

---

### DATA_FLOW

The data flows within Mediimate are designed to support a holistic patient journey and efficient operations. Here's a high-level overview of key data movements and relationships:

1.  **User Onboarding & Identity Propagation**:
    *   New users register via `authusers` (core credentials).
    *   A corresponding entry is created in `profiles` (basic details like name, phone, specialty if doctor).
    *   For patients, a `patients` record is created (detailed health profile).
    *   For clinic staff (doctors/admins), `clinicinvites` manages the invitation, leading to `clinicmembers` to establish affiliation, and `userroles` for access control.
    *   Doctors and patients can link via `linkrequests` (pending) -> `patientdoctorlinks` (approved/active), granting authorized access.

2.  **Care Plan & Program Management**:
    *   `programs` and `careplans` define reusable templates for health initiatives.
    *   A doctor (from `profiles`/`authusers`) assigns these templates to a patient (from `patients`), creating entries in `enrollments` (for programs) and `careplanassignments` (for care plans).
    *   Patient progress on care plans is tracked daily within `careplanassignments.day_logs`.

3.  **Health Tracking & Monitoring**:
    *   Patients log daily health data into `vitals`, `foodlogs`, `labresults`.
    *   These logs update `patientgamifications` (points, streaks) and can trigger `alerts` (e.g., for abnormal vital signs or low adherence).
    *   `labreports` and `patientdocuments` store uploaded medical files, which are processed by AI to generate `ai_summary` and `layman_summary`, linking back to `patients` and `doctors`.

4.  **Appointment Management**:
    *   `doctoravailabilities` defines recurring schedules for doctors (from `profiles`/`authusers`) at `clinics`.
    *   Patients (from `patients`/`profiles`) book `appointments` with doctors at clinics based on availability.
    *   On the day of the visit, `appointmentcheckins` tracks the physical presence and completion of the appointment.

5.  **AI & Conversational Interactions**:
    *   Patients interact with AI via `chatconversations` or `voiceconversations`.
    *   The `sessions` collection maintains the current `state` and `data` for ongoing conversations, providing context to the AI (e.g., `last_bot_message`).
    *   Information from these conversations can implicitly feed into other areas (e.g., triggering `alerts`, logging data to `vitals`/`foodlogs`).

6.  **Notifications & Feedback**:
    *   Various system events (e.g., new `enrollments`, `appointments` completion, `alerts` generation) trigger entries in `notifications` for specific `user_id`s and `emailnotificationlogs` for audit.
    *   After an `appointment` is completed, a `feedbackrequest` is generated for the `patient`.
    *   When the patient provides feedback, a `feedbacks` record is created, referencing the `appointment`, `patient`, and `doctor`.

7.  **Gamification & Rewards**:
    *   `patientgamifications` aggregates points and streaks based on `vitals`, `foodlogs`, `careplanassignments` progress, and `userweeklychallenges` completions.
    *   Achieving milestones or completing challenges leads to `milestonerewards` being issued to the `patient_id`.

---

### ENTITY_LOCATIONS

Here's where the core entities reside within the Mediimate system:

*   **Patients**:
    *   **`patients`**: Primary location for comprehensive health profiles (demographics, conditions, medications, assigned doctor/clinic, engagement tracking).
    *   **`profiles`**: Basic user profile information (full name, phone), linked to `authusers`.
    *   **`authusers`**: Core authentication credentials (email, password hash) and a unique `user_id`.
    *   Also appear in: `careplanassignments`, `chatconversations`, `enrollments`, `foodlogs`, `labreports`, `labresults`, `linkrequests`, `milestonerewards`, `notifications`, `patientdoctorlinks`, `patientdocuments`, `patientgamifications`, `patientvaultcodes`, `userweeklychallenges`, `vitals`, `voiceconversations` (as `patient_id` or `patient_user_id`).

*   **Doctors**:
    *   **`profiles`**: Basic user profile information (full name, doctor code, specialties), linked to `authusers`.
    *   **`authusers`**: Core authentication credentials (email, password hash) and a unique `user_id`.
    *   **`doctoravailabilities`**: Recurring availability schedules.
    *   Also appear in: `alerts`, `appointments`, `appointmentcheckins`, `careplanassignments`, `clinics` (created_by), `emailnotificationlogs` (as `to_user_id`), `enrollments`, `feedbacks`, `feedbackrequests`, `foodlogs`, `labreports`, `labresults`, `linkrequests`, `patientdoctorlinks`, `patientdocuments`, `patients` (as `doctor_id`), `programs` (as `doctor_id`).

*   **Consultations**:
    *   **`appointments`**: Scheduled consultations (date, time, patient, doctor, clinic, type, status).
    *   **`appointmentcheckins`**: Physical visit records for scheduled appointments (check-in/completion times).
    *   **`chatconversations`**: Transcripts of AI-driven text-based consultations.
    *   **`voiceconversations`**: Transcripts of AI-driven voice-based consultations.

*   **Plans / Programs**:
    *   **`programs`**: Templates/definitions for high-level healthcare programs (name, description, duration, type).
    *   **`careplans`**: Templates/definitions for specific, structured care plans (condition, duration, scoring rules, reward tiers, weekly themes).
    *   **`enrollments`**: Patient-specific instances of `programs` (patient_id, program_id, doctor_id, status, adherence).
    *   **`careplanassignments`**: Patient-specific instances of `careplans` (patient_id, careplan_id, doctor_id, daily logs, gamification progress).

*   **Sessions / Logs**:
    *   **`sessions`**: Stores the current state and contextual data for active conversational AI interactions (phone, state, temporary data).
    *   **`chatconversations`**: Full historical logs of AI chat interactions (messages, patient_id).
    *   **`voiceconversations`**: Full historical logs of AI voice interactions (messages, patient_id, duration).
    *   **`foodlogs`**: Detailed records of patient dietary intake.
    *   **`vitals`**: Individual vital sign measurements (blood pressure, heart rate, etc.).
    *   **`emailnotificationlogs`**: Audit trail of all sent email notifications.
    *   **`alerts`**: Records of patient health alerts generated by the system.
    *   **`appointmentcheckins`**: Operational logs for appointment visits.

---

### PATIENT_LIFECYCLE

The patient lifecycle in Mediimate follows a comprehensive journey from initial interest to ongoing care and follow-up, seamlessly integrating human care with digital tools.

**1. Onboarding & Registration:**
*   **Initial Interest:** A prospective user (patient or clinic) might fill out a form, creating a `contactleads` entry.
*   **User Account Creation:** The patient registers, creating an `authusers` record for authentication (email, password hash).
*   **Profile Setup:** A `profiles` entry is created with basic demographic info. If the user is a patient, a detailed `patients` record is established, capturing conditions, medications, and contact details.
*   **Clinic Affiliation:** If the patient is part of a specific clinic, they may be linked via `clinicmembers`.
*   **Doctor Assignment/Linking:** The patient is assigned a doctor (`patients.doctor_id`) or initiates a `linkrequests` to connect with a specific doctor. Upon approval, a `patientdoctorlinks` record formalizes the relationship, granting the doctor access to relevant patient data.
*   **Initial Documents:** Any existing medical documents (scans, previous reports) can be uploaded to `patientdocuments` and `labreports` for AI-driven summarization and structured data extraction.

**2. Treatment & Active Care:**
*   **Care Plan/Program Enrollment:** The assigned doctor reviews the patient's condition and enrolls them in a suitable `programs` or `careplans` template. This creates an `enrollments` or `careplanassignments` record, tracking the patient's progress through the program/plan, including daily logs (`careplanassignments.day_logs`).
*   **Appointment Scheduling:** The patient or doctor schedules `appointments` based on `doctoravailabilities`.
*   **Health Tracking & Monitoring:** Patients actively log `vitals`, `foodlogs`, and `labresults` through the app. These logs are stored and contribute to their `patientgamifications` profile (points, streaks, levels).
*   **AI-Assisted Support:** Patients can interact with AI health companions through `chatconversations` and `voiceconversations` for queries, reminders, and self-management advice. The `sessions` collection maintains conversational context.
*   **Alerts & Interventions:** The system constantly monitors patient data. If thresholds are breached (e.g., vital signs out of range, low adherence to care plan activities), `alerts` are generated for the doctor, and `notifications` are sent to both the patient and doctor.
*   **Medication Management:** Extracted medication data from `patientdocuments` or `labreports` can be used for reminders (tracked in `patients.reminders_sent_today`).
*   **Gamified Engagement:** Patients are motivated by `userweeklychallenges` and earn `milestonerewards` for achieving health milestones or adhering to their plans.

**3. Follow-up & Continuous Engagement:**
*   **Post-Appointment Feedback:** After an `appointment`, a `feedbackrequest` is sent to the patient. Their `feedbacks` provide valuable insights into service quality.
*   **Program Completion/Review:** Upon completion of a `program` or `careplan`, the `enrollments` or `careplanassignments` status is updated, and the patient's progress is reviewed by the doctor. New plans might be initiated.
*   **Reminders & Education:** The system sends automated `notifications` and `emailnotificationlogs` for follow-up appointments, medication reminders, health tips, and re-engagement prompts (tracked by `patients.last_food_log_reminder_date`, etc.).
*   **Ongoing Monitoring:** Patients continue to log health data, and the system continues to monitor for `alerts` and provide AI support, ensuring continuous care.
*   **Secure Access:** `patientvaultcodes` can be used for secure, temporary access to specific medical information, for example, when sharing with a new specialist.

This lifecycle demonstrates a continuous loop of assessment, intervention, monitoring, and engagement, supported by an integrated data ecosystem.

---

**Key Architectural Considerations:**

*   **Document-Oriented Flexibility**: MongoDB's schemaless nature allows for flexible data structures, evident in collections like `sessions.data` or embedded `messages` arrays in conversations, facilitating rapid evolution.
*   **Denormalization for Performance**: Fields like `doctor_name` in `patientdoctorlinks` or AI summaries directly embedded in `labreports`/`patientdocuments` indicate strategic denormalization to optimize read performance and reduce joins.
*   **AI Integration**: A dedicated AI module is evident through collections like `chatconversations`, `voiceconversations`, `sessions`, `labreports`, and `patientdocuments`, suggesting significant investment in intelligent processing and interaction.
*   **Event-Driven Triggers**: The description of `alerts` being *triggered by* other data (vitals, adherence) implies an event-driven architecture for real-time monitoring and reactions. Similarly, notifications and feedback requests are event-triggered.
*   **Gamification Engine**: `patientgamifications` and related collections point to a well-defined gamification engine that processes user actions into points, levels, and rewards, likely in an asynchronous manner.
*   **Auditing and Compliance**: Collections like `emailnotificationlogs` and `appointmentcheckins` (with timestamps) indicate a strong focus on creating auditable trails for actions and communications, crucial for healthcare regulations.
